# Overview | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

This environment provides a lightweight scripting layer for UI, rendering, memory analysis and interaction in Perception.cx. It uses **Lua** with core add-ons and PCX-specific APIs enabled by default.

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api#core-add-ons)

Core Add-ons

The following standard AngelScript modules are registered:

*   **base** — core Lua functions
    
*   **package** — `require()` and module loading
    
*   **coroutine** — coroutine creation & scheduling
    
*   **table** — table helpers (`insert`, `remove`, `sort`, ...)
    
*   **string** — pattern matching & string utilities
    
*   **math** — numeric functions
    
*   **utf8** — UTF-8 text helpers
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api#pcx-apis)

PCX APIs

Custom host APIs extend the scripting environment:

*   **Render API** — draw shapes, text, images, and gradients
    
*   **Input API** — mouse, keyboard, and scroll input
    
*   **Host Utilities** — logging and script lifecycle helpers
    
*   **Proc API** — memory inspection and manipulation
    
*   **GUI API** — create and interact with UI elements
    
*   **System API** — CPU info, instruction utilities, disassembly
    
*   **Net API** — HTTP, HTTPS, and WebSocket networking
    
*   **File System API** — read, write, and manage files/folders
    
*   **Extended Math API** — vectors, matrices, quaternions, and math helpers
    
*   **Engine Specific API** — read engine specific structures easier
    
*   **Json API**
    
*   **Utilities** — encoding, decoding, etc
    

[NextLife Cycle](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle)

Last updated 19 days ago

*   [Core Add-ons](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api#core-add-ons)

# Life Cycle | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

Every Lua script **must define** an entry function:

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle#main)

**main()**

Copy

    function main()
        ...
        return number
    end

Return Value

Meaning

**\> 0**

Script stays active **only if** `on_frame()` exists.

**≤ 0**

Script unloads immediately after `main()` finishes.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle#on_frame)

**on\_frame()**

Copy

    function on_frame()
        ...
    end

Behavior

Meaning

**Missing**

Script unloads right after `main()` (even if it returned > 0).

**Exists**

Runs every frame. Returning **≤ 0** unloads the script.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle#on_unload)

on\_unload()

Copy

    function on_unload()
        ...
    end

*   Called once **when the script is about to be unloaded**.
    
*   Use this to clean up state, save data, etc.
    
*   Cannot prevent the script from unloading
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle#execution-flow)

◆ Execution Flow

1.  The engine runs the script’s `main()` function.
    
2.  After `main()` returns:
    
    *   If return value **≤ 0** → script unloads.
        
    *   If return value **\> 0**:
        
        *   If `on_frame()` exists → script becomes persistent.
            
        *   If `on_frame()` is missing → script unloads immediately.
            
        
    
3.  For persistent scripts, `on_frame()` runs every frame until:
    
    *   It returns **≤ 0**, or
        
    *   The script is manually unloaded.
        
    
4.  When the script is unloading, `on_unload()` is called once (if defined)
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle#example-1-persistent-script)

◆ Example #1 — Persistent Script

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle#example-2-one-shot-script)

◆ Example #2 — One-shot Script

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle#engine-notes)

◆ Engine Notes

*   `main()` is **required**.
    
*   `on_frame()` is **optional**, but required for a script to stay active.
    
*   Returning **≤ 0** from either function unloads the script.
    
*   No infinite loops — frame updates are handled by the engine.
    

[PreviousOverview](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api)
[NextEngine](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine)

Last updated 22 days ago

*   [on\_unload()](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle#on_unload)
    
*   [◆ Execution Flow](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle#execution-flow)
    
*   [◆ Example #1 — Persistent Script](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle#example-1-persistent-script)
    
*   [◆ Example #2 — One-shot Script](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle#example-2-one-shot-script)

Copy

    function main()
        log("Persistent script.")
        return 1
    end
    
    function on_frame()
        log("Tick")
    end

Copy

    function main()
        log("This runs once.")
        return 1   -- still unloads because on_frame() is missing
    end

# Input API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The Input API provides access to mouse, keyboard, and UI-hover information from Lua scripts. These functions are intended to be used inside `on_frame()`.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#mouse-input)

🖱 Mouse Input

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#mouse-position)

Mouse Position

Copy

    x, y = get_mouse_pos()

Returns the cursor position **inside the game/overlay window**.

Copy

    x, y = get_mouse_pos_desktop()

Returns the cursor position in **desktop/screen coordinates**.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#mouse-delta)

Mouse Delta

Copy

    dx, dy = get_mouse_delta()

Movement since last frame in overlay space.

Copy

    dx, dy = get_mouse_delta_desktop()

Movement since last frame in desktop space.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#scroll-wheel)

Scroll Wheel

Copy

    amount = get_scroll_delta()

Positive for scroll up, negative for scroll down.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#movement-event)

Movement Event

Returns `true` if the mouse moved this frame.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#hover-detection)

Hover Detection

Returns `true` if the mouse is inside the rectangle `(x, y, w, h)`.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#keyboard-input)

⌨️ Keyboard Input

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#key-down)

Key Down

Returns `true` while key is held.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#raw-down)

Raw Down

Reflects OS-level down state before filtering.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#fired)

Fired

Behaves like text input

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#toggle)

Toggle

Toggles each time the key is pressed (flip-flop behavior).

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#single-press)

Single Press

True only on the **first frame** the key is pressed.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#previous-state)

Previous State

State from the previous frame.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#full-key-state)

🔍 Full Key State

Returns all internal state fields for a virtual key.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#keys-down-list)

🧩 Keys Down List

Returns a Lua table of all currently pressed virtual keys.

Example:

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#text-input-and-key-names)

📝 Text Input & Key Names

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#recent-typed-characters)

Recent Typed Characters

Returns a string of recently typed characters (from your internal text buffer).

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#key-name)

Key Name

Returns a readable name like `"SPACE"`, `"A"`, `"SHIFT"`.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#example)

📌 Example


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#notes)

💡 Notes


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `vk` refers to Windows Virtual-Key codes (e.g., `0x41` = `'A'`, `0x20` = Space).
    
*   The Input API is frame-based and intended to be called from inside `on_frame()`.
    
*   `get_recent_key_input()` is ideal for text input boxes or consoles.
    

[PreviousRender API](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api)
[NextProc API](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api)

Last updated 26 days ago

*   [🖱 Mouse Input](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#mouse-input)
    
*   [⌨️ Keyboard Input](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#keyboard-input)
    
*   [🔍 Full Key State](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#full-key-state)
    
*   [🧩 Keys Down List](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#keys-down-list)
    
*   [📝 Text Input & Key Names](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#text-input-and-key-names)
    
*   [📌 Example](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#example)
    
*   [💡 Notes](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#notes)
    

Copy

    moved = mouse_movement_received()

Copy

    hovered = is_hovered(x, y, w, h) --overlay window

Copy

    down = key_down(vk)

Copy

    raw = key_raw_down(vk)

Copy

    fired = key_fired(vk)

Copy

    toggle = key_toggle(vk)

Copy

    single = key_singlepress(vk)

Copy

    prev = key_prev_down(vk)

Copy

    raw_down, down, fired, toggle, single, prev =
        get_key_state(vk)

Copy

    keys = get_keys_down()

Copy

    for i, vk in ipairs(get_keys_down()) do
        log("Down: " .. get_key_name(vk))
    end

Copy

    txt = get_recent_key_input()

Copy

    name = get_key_name(vk)

Copy

    local font = 0
    local frame = 0
    local last_keys = ""
    
    function main()
        log("Lua Input Test Script Loaded!")
        font = get_font20()
        return 1
    end
    
    function on_frame()
        frame = frame + 1
        
        local vw, vh = get_view()
        local scale = get_view_scale()
        
        local mx, my = get_mouse_pos()
        local dx, dy = get_mouse_delta()
        local scroll = get_scroll_delta()
        
        local keys = get_keys_down()
        local recent = get_recent_key_input()
        
        -- Panel
        local w = 450 * scale
        local h = 300 * scale
        local x = 20 * scale
        local y = 20 * scale
        
        draw_rect_filled(
            x, y, w, h,
            20, 20, 25, 220,
            8 * scale,
            RR_TOP_LEFT | RR_TOP_RIGHT | RR_BOTTOM_LEFT | RR_BOTTOM_RIGHT
            )
        
        draw_rect(
            x, y, w, h,
            60, 120, 255, 255,
            2 * scale,
            8 * scale,
            RR_TOP_LEFT | RR_TOP_RIGHT | RR_BOTTOM_LEFT | RR_BOTTOM_RIGHT
            )
        
        local function text(label, value, ox, oy)
            draw_text(
                label .. value,
                x + 10 * scale, y + oy * scale,
                255, 255, 255, 255,
                font,
                TE_SHADOW,
                0,0,0,180,
                1.0,
                true
                )
        end
        
        text("Mouse Pos: ", string.format("%0.1f, %0.1f", mx, my), 10, 10)
        text("Mouse Delta: ", string.format("%0.2f, %0.2f", dx, dy), 10, 40)
        text("Scroll: ", tostring(scroll), 10, 70)
        
        -- Hover test
        local hx, hy, hw, hh = vw*0.5 - 50*scale, vh*0.5 - 50*scale, 100*scale, 100*scale
        local hovered = is_hovered(hx, hy, hw, hh)
        
        draw_rect_filled(
            hx, hy, hw, hh,
            hovered and 60 or 30,
            hovered and 200 or 60,
            hovered and 80 or 60,
            240,
            8*scale,
            RR_TOP_LEFT | RR_BOTTOM_RIGHT
            )
        
        text("Hovered (center box): ", hovered and "true" or "false", 10, 100)
        
        -- Key states
        local space_down = key_down(0x20)
        local space_name = get_key_name(0x20) or "?"
        
        text("SPACE down: ", tostring(space_down), 10, 130)
        text("SPACE name: ", space_name, 10, 190)
        
        -- Keys currently down
        local kd = ""
        for i,vk in ipairs(keys) do
            kd = kd .. get_key_name(vk) .. " "
        end  
        text("Keys down: ", kd, 10, 220)
        
        -- Recent typed characters
        if recent ~= "" then
            last_keys = recent
        end
        text("Recent typed: ", last_keys, 10, 250)
    end
    
    function on_unload()
        log("Lua Input Test Script Unloaded")
    end

---

# Render API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#constants)

Constants

Copy

    RR_TOP_LEFT
    RR_TOP_RIGHT
    RR_BOTTOM_LEFT
    RR_BOTTOM_RIGHT

Rectangle corner rounding flags (bitmask), used with `rounding_flags` in rect functions.

Copy

    TE_NONE
    TE_OUTLINE
    TE_SHADOW
    TE_GLOW

Text effects used by `draw_text`.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#viewport)

Viewport

Copy

    w, h = get_view()
    scale = get_view_scale()
    fps = get_fps()

*   `get_view()` — returns the current viewport width and height in pixels.
    
*   `get_view_scale()` — returns a reference scale factor (useful for DPI-aware sizes).
    
*   `get_fps()`
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#shapes)

Shapes

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#rectangle-outline)

Rectangle (outline)

Draws a rounded rectangle outline.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#rectangle-filled)

Rectangle (filled)

Draws a filled rounded rectangle.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#line)

Line

Draws a line from `(x1, y1)` to `(x2, y2)`.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#arc)

Arc

Draws an arc or pie-slice centered at `(cx, cy)`.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#circle)

Circle

Draws a circle centered at `(cx, cy)`.

*   If `filled == true`, draws a filled circle.
    
*   Otherwise draws an outlined circle.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#triangle)

Triangle

Draws a triangle using the three points `(ax, ay)`, `(bx, by)`, `(cx, cy)`.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#polygon)

Polygon

*   `xy_pairs` — Lua table of floats: `{ x1, y1, x2, y2, x3, y3, ... }`.
    
*   `count_pairs` — optional; if `nil` or `0`, uses the whole table.
    

Draws a polyline or filled polygon.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#four-corner-gradient)

Four-Corner Gradient

Draws a rectangle with independent colors per corner:

*   top-left: `(tlr, tlg, tlb, tla)`
    
*   top-right: `(trr, trg, trb, tra)`
    
*   bottom-left: `(blr, blg, blb, bla)`
    
*   bottom-right: `(brr, brg, brb, bra)`
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#bitmaps)

Bitmaps

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#create-bitmap)

Create bitmap

*   `data` — Lua table of `uint8` values (byte buffer).
    
*   Returns a handle `bmp` that can be passed to `draw_bitmap`.
    
*   Returns `0` on failure.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#draw-bitmap)

Draw bitmap

Draws a bitmap tinted with color `(r, g, b, a)`.

*   `bmp` — handle returned by `create_bitmap`.
    
*   `rounded` — if `true`, draws with rounded corners.
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#fonts-and-text)

Fonts & Text

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#built-in-fonts)

Built-in fonts

Returns a handle to a default font at a given size.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#create-font-from-file)

Create font from file

*   `path` — filesystem path or font name.
    
*   `size` — font size in pixels.
    
*   `anti_aliased` — `true` for smooth text, `false` for pixel-style rendering (boolean).
    
*   `load_color` — `true` to enable color glyphs (emoji / color fonts), `false` for standard monochrome glyphs (boolean).
    
*   Returns a font handle or `0` on failure.
    

The function searches for fonts inside the API directory (e.g. `verdana_custom.ttf`, `fonts/verdana_custom.ttf`) and may fall back to system font locations. If a font name matches a system font, that one may be loaded instead— use unique names to prevent conflicts.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#create-font-from-memory)

Create font from memory

*   `label` — name/tag for the font (string).
    
*   `size` — font size in pixels.
    
*   `buf` — Lua table of `uint8` values (font binary data).
    
*   `anti_aliased` — `true` for smooth text, `false` for pixel-style rendering (boolean).
    
*   `load_color` — `true` to enable color glyphs (emoji / color fonts), `false` for standard monochrome glyphs (boolean).
    
*   Returns a font handle or `0` on failure.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#draw-text)

Draw text

*   `text` — string to draw.
    
*   `(r, g, b, a)` — text color.
    
*   `font` — font handle.
    
*   `effect` — one of `TE_NONE`, `TE_OUTLINE`, `TE_SHADOW`, `TE_GLOW`.
    
*   `(er, eg, eb, ea)` — effect color (e.g. shadow/outline color).
    
*   `effect_amount` — intensity scalar.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#text-metrics)

Text metrics

*   `get_text_size` — returns width/height of the rendered `text`.
    
*   `get_char_advance` — returns advance width for a single character (`wchar32`).
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#clipping)

Clipping

*   `clip_push` — pushes a rectangular clip region.
    
*   `clip_pop` — restores the previous clip region.
    

All drawing while a clip is active is restricted to the specified rectangle.

* * *

###

              r, g, b, a,

                         maxw, maxh)

Copy

    clip_pop()

Copy

    local font = 0
    local t = 0
    
    function main()
        log("Lua render example loaded.")
    
        -- Use built-in default font
        font = get_font20()
    
        return 1 -- keep script running
    end
    
    function on_frame()
        -- Get viewport
        local vw, vh = get_view()
        local scale  = get_view_scale()
    
        t = t + 1
    
        -- Panel size
        local w  = 260 * scale
        local h  = 120 * scale
        local cx = vw * 0.5
        local cy = vh * 0.5
        local x  = cx - w * 0.5
        local y  = cy - h * 0.5
    
        -- Background panel
        draw_rect_filled(
            x, y, w, h,
            30, 30, 40, 230,      -- r,g,b,a
            8.0 * scale,          -- rounding
            RR_TOP_LEFT | RR_TOP_RIGHT | RR_BOTTOM_LEFT | RR_BOTTOM_RIGHT
        )
    
        -- Outline
        draw_rect(
            x, y, w, h,
            80, 140, 255, 255,    -- r,g,b,a
            2.0 * scale,          -- thickness
            8.0 * scale,          -- rounding
            RR_TOP_LEFT | RR_TOP_RIGHT | RR_BOTTOM_LEFT | RR_BOTTOM_RIGHT
        )
    
        -- Animated accent bar
        local bar_h = 4 * scale
        draw_rect_filled(
            x, y - bar_h - 2 * scale, w, bar_h,
            120 + (t % 60), 80, 220, 255,
            2.0 * scale,
            RR_TOP_LEFT | RR_TOP_RIGHT
        )
    
        -- Text
        local title = "Lua Render API"
        local w_text, h_text = get_text_size(font, title, 1000, 1000)
    
        local tx = cx - w_text * 0.5
        local ty = cy - h_text * 0.5 - 10 * scale
    
        draw_text(
            title,
            tx, ty,
            255, 255, 255, 255,  -- text color
            font,
            TE_SHADOW,           -- effect
            0, 0, 0, 180,        -- effect color (shadow)
            1.0,                 -- effect amount
        )
    
        -- Subtitle
        local subtitle = "drawing from Lua 5.4.6"
        local sw, sh = get_text_size(font, subtitle, 1000, 1000)
        local sx = cx - sw * 0.5
        local sy = ty + h_text + 8 * scale
    
        draw_text(
            subtitle,
            sx, sy,
            180, 200, 255, 255,
            font,
            TE_NONE,
            0, 0, 0, 0,
            0.0
        )
    end
    
    function on_unload()
        log("Lua render example unloading.")
    end

---

# Engine | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The Engine provides three global logging helpers available in every Lua script. Each of them targets a different part of the UI and is intended for a different use-case.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#log-message-string)

**log(message: string)**

Send a standard UI log message (top-left overlay).

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#syntax)

**Syntax**

Copy

    log("message")

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#description)

**Description**

Adds a **styled notification log** to the engine’s **top-left UI log feed**. These logs appear with the same formatting as other engine notifications (fade-out timers, colors, etc.).

Use this for:

*   Showing player/script status
    
*   Informative messages the user should see
    
*   Non-spammy logs meant for gameplay HUD
    

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#parameters)

**Parameters**

Name

Type

Description

message

string

The text that appears in the UI log panel.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#examples)

**Examples**

Copy

    log("Script initialized.")
    log("Speed boost activated!")

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#overlay-output)

**Overlay Output**

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#log_error-message-string)

**log\_error(message: string)**

Send an error message to the UI log panel.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#syntax-1)

**Syntax**

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#description-1)

**Description**

Same as `log()`, but marked as an **error**, shown with an **error style**, prefixing the message with `**[LUA][ERR]**`.

Use this for:

*   Script mistakes
    
*   Missing data
    
*   Important failures that should be visible to users
    

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#parameters-1)

**Parameters**

Name

Type

Description

message

string

Error text to show in the UI log feed.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#examples-1)

**Examples**

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#overlay-output-1)

**Overlay Output**

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#log_console-message-string)

**log\_console(message: string)**

Append text to the debug console (persistent until cleared).

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#syntax-2)

**Syntax**

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#description-2)

**Description**

Writes text directly into the **script debugging console**, where messages accumulate continuously. This console is separate from the UI log panel and is intended purely for development and live debugging.

Use this for:

*   Repeated updates inside loops
    
*   Value tracing
    
*   Spammy or high-frequency debug output
    
*   Printing raw data structures
    
*   Debug logs you don’t want appearing in the UI overlay
    

Unlike `log()` and `log_error()`, **console output does not fade or disappear** — it continues to append until the user manually clears the console.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#parameters-2)

**Parameters**

Name

Type

Description

message

string

Text to append to the debug console.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#examples-2)

**Examples**

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#console-output)

**Console Output**

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#notes)

**Notes**

*   Best for development/debug use.
    
*   Not shown in the UI overlay.
    
*   Does not fade; accumulates until cleared.
    
*   Perfect for live script debugging.
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#get_user_name-string)

get\_user\_name(): string

Returns the current PCX username.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#syntax-3)

**Syntax**

[PreviousLife Cycle](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/life-cycle)
[NextRender API](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api)

Last updated 2 days ago

*   [log(message: string)](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#log-message-string)
    
*   [log\_error(message: string)](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#log_error-message-string)
    
*   [log\_console(message: string)](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#log_console-message-string)
    
*   [get\_user\_name(): string](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine#get_user_name-string)

    [LUA] Script initialized.
    [LUA] Speed boost activated!

# File System | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

**API Folder Location** : C:\\Users\\"UserName"\\Documents\\My Games\\

Filesystem API that allows scripts to read, write, and manage files **only inside the main scripting directory**.

Scripts **cannot** access, modify, create, or query files **outside** this directory. All paths must be **relative** and are automatically sandboxed for safety.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/file-system#overview)

**Overview**


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The filesystem API provides the following capabilities:

*   Create files
    
*   Create directories
    
*   Read files
    
*   Check if a file exists
    
*   List files or directories
    
*   Delete files
    
*   Delete directories
    

All functions operate only on paths **relative to the script directory**.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/file-system#path-rules)

**Path Rules**


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To ensure safety and consistency:

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/file-system#paths-must-be-relative)

✔ Paths must be relative

Absolute paths such as:

are not allowed.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/file-system#parent-directory-traversal-is-not-allowed)

✔ Parent-directory traversal is not allowed

Paths cannot contain:

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/file-system#scripts-cannot-escape-the-main-scripting-directory)

✔ Scripts cannot escape the main scripting directory

Every operation is automatically constrained to the script directory.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/file-system#global-functions)

**Global Functions**


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

All filesystem functions are available as **global Lua functions**.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/file-system#create_file-path-data-boolean)

`create_file(path, [data]) → boolean`

Creates or overwrites a file.

####

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/file-system#example-1)

Example:

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/file-system#read_file-path-boolean-string)

`read_file(path) → boolean, string`

Reads a file and returns `(success, contents)`.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/file-system#example-2)

Example:

    function main()
        print("=== FS TEST START ===")
    
        create_directory("fs_tests")
        create_file("fs_tests/test.txt", "hello test")
    
        local ok, data = read_file("fs_tests/test.txt")
        print("read ok:", ok, "data:", data)
    
        local ok_q, items = query_directory("fs_tests")
        if ok_q then
            for _, name in ipairs(items) do
                print(" -", name)
            end
        end
    
        delete_file("fs_tests/test.txt")
        delete_directory("fs_tests")
    
        print("=== FS TEST END ===")
        return 0;
    end

# Utilities | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The `util` module provides fast Base64, Hex, and URL encoding/decoding helpers for Lua scripts.

All functions operate on **raw byte strings**, not UTF-8 text, so they safely support:

*   Binary data
    
*   Network packets
    
*   Ciphertext
    
*   Hashes
    
*   Buffers containing `\0` bytes
    
*   Arbitrary byte sequences
    

The module is registered globally as:

Copy

    util = {
        base64_encode = function(str) end,
        base64_decode = function(str) end,
        hex_encode    = function(str) end,
        hex_decode    = function(str) end,
        url_encode    = function(str) end,
        url_decode    = function(str) end,
    }

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#base64-functions)

Base64 Functions


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#util.base64_encode-str)

`util.base64_encode(str)`

Encodes a raw byte string into Base64 text.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#parameters)

Parameters

Name

Type

Description

string

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#returns)

*   Base64 string
    

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#example)

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#error-examples)

Error Examples

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#url-encode-decode)

URL Encode / Decode


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Matches standard percent-encoding:

*   Safe characters stay as-is: `A–Z a–z 0–9 - _ . ~`
    
*   Everything else becomes `%XX`
    

`+` is **not** treated as space. Binary bytes are preserved.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#util.url_encode-str)

`util.url_encode(str)`

Encodes text for safe URL usage.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#example-4)

Example

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#util.url_decode-str)

`util.url_decode(str)`

Decodes `%XX` sequences back into bytes.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#example-5)

Example

Invalid `%` sequences are returned literally.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#roundtrip-examples)

Roundtrip Examples


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#base64-roundtrip)

Base64 roundtrip

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#hex-roundtrip)

Hex roundtrip

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#url-roundtrip)

URL roundtrip

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#binary-safety)

Binary Safety


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

All `util.*` functions:

*   correctly handle `\0` bytes
    
*   accept arbitrary binary input
    
*   never corrupt data
    
*   do not assume UTF-8
    
*   support large buffers
    

Tested with byte sizes from 1 → 256 without corruption.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#summary)

Summary


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Function

Description

`util.base64_encode(str)`

Encode bytes → Base64

`util.base64_decode(str)`

Decode Base64 → bytes (or nil+error)

`util.hex_encode(str)`

Encode bytes → uppercase hex

`util.hex_decode(str)`

Decode hex → bytes (or nil+error)

`util.url_encode(str)`

Percent-encode unsafe characters

`util.url_decode(str)`

Decode `%XX` → bytes

Copy

    local out = util.base64_encode("hello")
    print(out)   --> aGVsbG8=

Copy

    local raw, err = util.base64_decode("aGVsbG8=")
    if raw then
        print(raw)   --> hello
    else
        print("Decode failed:", err)
    end

Copy

    local v, err = util.base64_decode("!!!!bad!!!!")
    -- v   == nil
    -- err == "Invalid base64 character"

Copy

    local out = util.hex_encode("ABC")
    print(out)   --> 414243

Copy

    local raw = util.hex_decode("414243")
    print(raw)   --> ABC

Copy

    util.hex_decode("ABC")
    -- nil, "Hex string length must be even"
    
    util.hex_decode("GGGG")
    -- nil, "Invalid hex character"

Copy

    local enc = util.url_encode("hello world! 100% ok?")
    print(enc)
    -- "hello%20world%21%20100%25%20ok%3F"

Copy

    local dec = util.url_decode("name=John%20Doe&msg=hi%21")
    print(dec)
    -- "name=John Doe&msg=hi!"

Copy

    local original = "hello world"
    local enc = util.base64_encode(original)
    local dec = util.base64_decode(enc)
    assert(dec == original)

Copy

    local original = "hello world"
    local hex = util.hex_encode(original)
    local raw = util.hex_decode(hex)
    assert(raw == original)

Copy

    local original = "[email protected]&msg=hello!"
    local enc = util.url_encode(original)
    local dec = util.url_decode(enc)
    assert(dec == original)

# Proc API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

This API lets scripts inspect and modify the memory of external processes via a `process` userdata. Handles are created with `ref_process(...)` and released with `deref_process(process)`.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#process-handles)

🔑 Process Handles

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#userdata-type)

Userdata Type

All functions operate on a `process` userdata created by `ref_process`.

Copy

    -- Get a process handle by PID
    local proc = ref_process(1234)
    
    -- Get a process handle by name
    local proc = ref_process("notepad.exe")

If the process is not found, `ref_process` returns `nil`.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#referencing-releasing)

Referencing / Releasing

Copy

    process = ref_process(pid_or_name)   -- global
    deref_process(process)               -- global

*   `ref_process(pid)` – `pid` is a number (Windows PID).
    
*   `ref_process("name.exe")` – search by executable name.
    
*   `deref_process(process)` – releases the reference; the userdata becomes invalid.
    
*   You must also call `deref_process` if `process:alive()` returns `false`.
    

> Each Lua script keeps its own list of referenced processes internally. Always call `deref_process(proc)` when you’re done.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#process-info)

🧬 Process Info

*   `base_address()` – Image base address of the process.
    
*   `peb()` – Address of the process’ PEB.
    
*   `pid()` – Process ID.
    
*   `alive()` - Determines whether the process is currently alive and running.
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#scalar-reads)

📖 Scalar Reads

All addresses are **virtual addresses** in the target process.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#unsigned-integers)

Unsigned Integers

Reads unsigned integers from `addr`.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#signed-integers)

Signed Integers

Reads signed integers from `addr`.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#floating-point)

Floating Point

Reads floating point values from `addr`.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#scalar-writes)

✏️ Scalar Writes

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#unsigned-integers-1)

Unsigned Integers

Writes an unsigned integer at `addr`. Returns `true` on success.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#signed-integers-1)

Signed Integers

Writes a signed integer at `addr`.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#floating-point-1)

Floating Point

Writes `float` / `double`.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#strings)

🔤 Strings

Read and write null-terminated strings from the remote process.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#read-strings)

Read Strings

*   `rs` – Reads up to `max_chars` characters from `addr`.
    
*   `rws` – Reads a wide string and converts it to a Lua UTF-8 string.
    
*   If nothing valid is read, an empty string is returned.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#write-strings)

Write Strings

*   `ws` – Writes `text` bytes plus a terminating `\0`.
    
*   `wws` – Converts `text` to UTF-16 and writes plus wide `\0`.
    

Returns `true` on success.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#raw-memory-byte-tables)

📦 Raw Memory (byte tables)

Use Lua tables of bytes (`1..N`, values `0–255`) for bulk reads / writes.

*   `rvm` – Returns a new table of length `size` filled with bytes from `addr`.
    
*   `wvm` – Writes all bytes in `byte_table` to `addr`. Returns `true` if all bytes are written.
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#simd-helpers)

🧮 SIMD Helpers

Convenience helpers for 16/32/64-byte SIMD vectors (raw bytes).

All values are plain bytes (`0–255`). `wXXX` returns `false` if the table is too short or the write fails.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#modules-and-pattern-scanning)

📦 Modules & Pattern Scanning

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#module-lookup)

Module Lookup

*   `name` – Module name, e.g. `"notepad.exe"`, `"client.dll"`.
    
*   Returns `base, size` on success.
    
*   Returns `nil` if the module is not found.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#code-pattern-scan)

Code Pattern Scan

*   `search_start` – Starting address.
    
*   `search_size` – Number of bytes to scan.
    
*   `signature` – Pattern string, e.g. `"48 8B ?? ?? ?? 89"` (same format as your internal pattern scanner).
    

Returns:

*   `addr` – Address of the first match, or `0` if not found.
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#example-scanning-notepad-lua)

🔍 Example: Scanning Notepad (Lua)

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#proc-read_struct)

`proc:read_struct`


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Reads a **single C-style structure** from the target process using a descriptor table.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#descriptor)

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#proc-read_struct_array)

📘 `proc:read_struct_array`


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Reads an **array of structures** from the target process.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#signature-1)

**Signature**

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#parameters-1)

**Parameters**

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#base_address-1)

`**base_address**`

Address of the **first** element in the array.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#count)

`**count**`

Number of array elements to read.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#struct_size)

`**struct_size**`

Size in bytes of each array element.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#descriptor-1)

`**descriptor**`

Same descriptor table used with `read_struct`.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#returns-1)

**Returns**

A **1-based Lua array**, where each element is a struct table:

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#example-reading-a-player-array)

**Example – Reading a Player Array**

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#virtual-memory-allocation)

Virtual Memory Allocation

These functions let you allocate and manage RWX memory inside the target process. They are intended for advanced use; you are fully responsible for tracking and freeing any allocations you create.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#important-memory-management-notes-must-read)

🔴 Important Memory Management Notes (MUST READ!)

These points are critical for using `alloc_vm` safely:

*   **Control Flow Guard** If the target process has Control Flow Guard (CFG) enabled and you intend to execute code from this region, CFG may block all jumps and calls into the allocated memory. To avoid this, CFG must be fully disabled for the target process. Be aware that disabling CFG reduces the security of the device.
    
*   **Allocations are not automatically freed.** Every allocation you create must be manually released using `free_vm()`. If you lose track of an allocation, the memory will remain reserved until the target process exits.
    
*   **Allocations persist for the lifetime of the target process.** Memory created with `alloc_vm` is automatically released only when the **target process** itself closes.
    
*   **Closing the Perception overlay will clear all allocations.** When the overlay is closed, Perception will clean up every RWX allocation for _all_ processes currently referenced. If you need an allocation to stay alive, **do not close the overlay** while that memory is being used.
    
*   **Repeated unfreed allocations can exhaust physical memory.** If you repeatedly allocate memory without freeing it, these leaks will accumulate and can eventually **consume all available physical RAM**, potentially degrading system performance or causing instability. If you are writing an injector make sure your inject frees the memory
    
*   **If you are writing an injector, you must free allocated memory.** Any injector, loader, or external tool that allocates memory through `alloc_vm` is responsible for freeing it once the memory is no longer needed. Failing to do so will leave permanent physical memory leaks until the target process exits.
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#functions)

Functions

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#uint64-proc-alloc_vm-size)

`uint64 proc:alloc_vm(size)`

Allocates a block of **read–write–execute (RWX)** memory inside the target process and returns its base address.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#parameters-2)

Parameters

*   **size** — Size of the allocation in bytes.
    

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#returns-2)

Returns

*   Base address of the allocation on success.
    
*   `0` on failure.
    

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#notes)

Notes

*   Allocated memory is **not tied to any module** and is **not discoverable** through helpers like module queries or pattern scans. You must store and manage the returned address yourself.
    
*   The memory is RWX. If the target process uses **Control Flow Guard (CFG)** and you intend to execute code from this region, CFG may block jumps/calls unless the target allows it.
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#bool-proc-free_vm-address)

`bool proc:free_vm(address)`

Frees a region previously allocated with `proc:alloc_vm()`.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#parameters-3)

Parameters

*   **address** — The exact base address returned by `alloc_vm`.
    

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#returns-3)

Returns

*   `true` if the region was successfully freed.
    
*   `false` if the address is invalid or the free fails.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#export-lookup-process-get_proc_address)

🔗 Export Lookup – `process:get_proc_address`

Resolves the address of an **exported function or symbol** inside a module in the target process.

*   `module_base` Base address of the module **inside the target process**. Typically obtained from:
    
    *   `process:base_address()`, or
        
    *   `local base, size = process:get_module("module_name.dll")`.
        
    
*   `export_name` Name of the exported function/symbol, e.g. `"Sleep"`, `"CreateFileW"`, `"DllMain"`.
    

**Returns**

*   Absolute **virtual address** of the exported symbol in the target process (as a Lua integer).
    
*   `0` if the export is not found or the arguments are invalid.
    

**Notes**

*   This walks the module’s **export table only** – it does _not_ look at imports or IAT.
    
*   The returned address is suitable for:
    
    *   Remote call stubs / shellcode.
        
    *   Manual thunks that jump directly to an API inside the target module.
        
    

**Example**

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#import-table-iat-slot-lookup-process-get_import_rdata_address)

🧷 Import Table (IAT) Slot Lookup – `process:get_import_rdata_address`

Resolves the **address of the import table entry** (IAT slot) for a given imported function inside a module.

This does **not** return the function’s address itself – it returns the address of the **pointer stored in** `**.rdata**` **/ IAT**. You can then read or patch that pointer for IAT hooks.

*   `module_base` Base address of the module whose imports you want to inspect/patch (usually the main EXE or a specific DLL), e.g. from `process:get_module(...)`.
    
*   `import_name` Name of the imported function (as it appears in the import table), e.g. `"Sleep"`, `"MessageBoxW"`.
    

**Returns**

*   Address of the **IAT entry** (pointer-sized slot) as a Lua integer.
    
*   `0` if the import cannot be found or arguments are invalid.
    

**Typical usage**

*   Read the current imported function pointer:
    
*   Install a simple IAT hook (patch the slot to point to your stub):
    

**Notes**

*   Only sees functions present in the module’s **static import table**.
    
*   Manually resolved APIs (e.g. `GetProcAddress` into some custom region) will **not** show up here.
    
*   Designed for **IAT hooks** and for shellcode that wants to call through the same import slot as the module.

Copy

    process:base_address()  --> number (uint64)
    process:peb()           --> number (uint64)
    process:pid()           --> number (uint)
    process:alive()         --> bool

    process:ru8(addr)   --> uint8
    process:ru16(addr)  --> uint16
    process:ru32(addr)  --> uint32
    process:ru64(addr)  --> uint64

Copy

    process:r8(addr)   --> int8
    process:r16(addr)  --> int16
    process:r32(addr)  --> int32
    process:r64(addr)  --> int64

Copy

    process:rf64(addr) --> double

Copy

    process:wu16(addr, value) --> bool
    process:wu32(addr, value) --> bool
    process:wu64(addr, value) --> bool

Copy

    process:w8(addr,  value) --> bool
    process:w16(addr, value) --> bool
    process:w32(addr, value) --> bool
    process:w64(addr, value) --> bool

Copy

    process:wf32(addr, value) --> bool
    process:wf64(addr, value) --> bool

Copy

    process:rs(addr,  max_chars) --> string    -- ANSI / UTF-8 style
    process:rws(addr, max_chars) --> string    -- UTF-16 wide -> Lua string

Copy

    process:ws(addr,  text) --> bool   -- ANSI / UTF-8
    process:wws(addr, text) --> bool   -- UTF-16 wide

Copy

    process:rvm(addr, size)          --> { byte1, byte2, ... }
    process:wvm(addr, byte_table)    --> bool

Copy

    process:r128(addr)        --> { b1..b16 }
    process:r256(addr)        --> { b1..b32 }
    process:r512(addr)        --> { b1..b64 }
    
    process:w128(addr, t16)   --> bool  -- t16 length >= 16
    process:w256(addr, t32)   --> bool  -- t32 length >= 32
    process:w512(addr, t64)   --> bool  -- t64 length >= 64

Copy

    local base, size = process:get_module(name)

Copy

    local addr = process:find_code_pattern(search_start, search_size, signature)

Copy

    function main()
        log("==== LUA PROC API TEST START ====")
    
        local proc = ref_process("notepad.exe")
        if not proc then
            log("[-] Failed to ref notepad.exe")
            return
        end
    
        local pid   = proc:pid()
        local base  = proc:base_address()
        local peb   = proc:peb()
    
        log(string.format("[+] Referenced Notepad: pid=%d", pid))
        log(string.format("    Base Address = 0x%016X", base))
        log(string.format("    PEB          = 0x%016X", peb))
    
        -- DOS header
        local b0 = proc:ru8(base)
        local b1 = proc:ru8(base + 1)
        log(string.format("Header bytes: %02X %02X", b0, b1))
    
        -- First 16 bytes as hex
        local raw = proc:rvm(base, 16)
        local hex = {}
        for i = 1, #raw do
            hex[#hex+1] = string.format("%02X", raw[i])
        end
        log("DOS header (16 bytes): " .. table.concat(hex, " "))
    
        -- Module + pattern scan
        local mod_base, mod_size = proc:get_module("notepad.exe")
        if mod_base then
            log(string.format("Module Base = 0x%016X", mod_base))
            log(string.format("Module Size = 0x%X",    mod_size))
    
            local addr = proc:find_code_pattern(mod_base, mod_size, "4D 5A")
            log(string.format("Pattern '4D 5A' found at 0x%016X", addr))
        else
            log("[-] get_module('notepad.exe') failed")
        end
    
        -- SIMD round-trip (128-bit)
        local v128 = proc:r128(base)
        local ok = proc:w128(base, v128)
        log("w128 ok? " .. tostring(ok))
    
        deref_process(proc)
        log("==== LUA PROC API TEST END ====")
    end

Copy

    table proc:read_struct(uint64 base_address, table descriptor)

Copy

    field_name = {
        offset = <byte offset>,
        type   = "<field type>"
    }

Copy

    local t = proc:read_struct(addr, DESC)
    
    print(t.health)
    print(t.pos_x)

Copy

    local DOS_HEADER = {
        e_magic  = { offset = 0x00, type = "u16" },
        e_lfanew = { offset = 0x3C, type = "u32" },
    }
    
    local proc = ref_process("notepad.exe")
    local base = proc:get_module("notepad.exe")
    
    local dos = proc:read_struct(base, DOS_HEADER)
    
    log_console(string.format("e_magic  = 0x%04X", dos.e_magic))
    log_console(string.format("e_lfanew = 0x%08X", dos.e_lfanew))

Copy

    table proc:read_struct_array(
        uint64 base_address,
        integer count,
        integer struct_size,
        table descriptor
    )

Copy

    local arr = proc:read_struct_array(addr, 10, 0x140, DESC)
    print(arr[1].health)

Copy

    local PLAYER = {
        health = { offset = 0x10, type = "i32" },
        armor  = { offset = 0x14, type = "i32" },
        pos_x  = { offset = 0x30, type = "f32" },
    }
    
    local base = 0x12345678
    local size = 0x140
    local count = 5
    
    local players = proc:read_struct_array(base, count, size, PLAYER)
    
    for i, p in ipairs(players) do
        log_console(string.format(
            "Player %d: hp=%d armor=%d x=%.1f",
            i, p.health, p.armor, p.pos_x
        ))
    end

Copy

    bool   proc:free_vm(uint64 address)

    local proc = ref_process("notepad.exe")
    if not proc then return end
    
    local kbase, ksize = proc:get_module("KERNEL32.DLL")
    if kbase then
        local addr_sleep = proc:get_proc_address(kbase, "Sleep")
        log(string.format("Sleep @ 0x%016X", addr_sleep))

    deref_process(proc)

    slot_addr = process:get_import_rdata_address(module_base, import_name)

    local slot = proc:get_import_rdata_address(mod_base, "Sleep")
    if slot ~= 0 then
        local current = proc:ru64(slot)   -- current function pointer
        log(string.format("IAT[Sleep] = 0x%016X", current))
    end

Copy

    local slot = proc:get_import_rdata_address(mod_base, "Sleep")
    if slot ~= 0 then
        -- 'stub_addr' is an RWX address you allocated with proc:alloc_vm(...)
        local ok = proc:wu64(slot, stub_addr)
        log("IAT hook applied? " .. tostring(ok))
    end

# Engine | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#overview)

⚙️ Overview

A callback is a **script function** that executes repeatedly on a background thread created by the engine. Each callback receives a unique **callback ID** (integer) and runs at a defined interval in milliseconds.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#registration-functions)

🧩 Registration Functions

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#register-callback)

Register Callback

Copy

    int register_callback(const __Internal_CallbackFn@ fn, int every_ms, int data_index)

Registers a new recurring callback function. The engine launches a lightweight thread that periodically invokes your callback, passing both its unique ID and the `data_index` you supplied.

**Parameter**

**Type**

**Description**

`fn`

`__Internal_CallbackFn@`

Function pointer to the callback (takes two integer arguments — the callback ID and the data index).

`every_ms`

`int`

Delay in milliseconds between callback executions.

`data_index`

`int`

User-defined integer value forwarded to your callback each time it runs. This can represent a dataset slot, UI layer, or logic group.

**Returns:** A unique callback ID (`int`) if successful, or `0` on failure. Drawing And Input is unique for each thread.

> 🧠 The callback executes in its own thread. Each iteration:
> 
> 1.  Begins input collection
>     
> 2.  Executes your callback function
>     
> 3.  Submits the current draw list
>     
> 4.  Ends input and sleeps for `every_ms`
>     

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#unregister-callback)

Unregister Callback

Stops a previously registered callback and terminates its thread.

Parameter

Type

Description

id

int

The callback ID returned by `register_callback`.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#callback-function-type)

🧠 Callback Function Type

The callback function type is defined internally by the engine:

Your script callback must accept **two integer parameters**:

**Parameter**

**Type**

**Description**

`callback_id`

`int`

The callback ID returned by `register_callback`. This uniquely identifies the running callback instance.

`data_index`

`int`

A user-defined or engine-supplied index value associated with this callback execution. Can be used to differentiate multiple data contexts handled by the same callback.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#example)

Example

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#logging-helper)

🪵 Logging Helper

Example:

* * *

get\_username(): string

Returns the current PCX username as a string.

[NextRender API](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/render-api)

Copy

Copy

    void on_update(int callback_id, int data_index)
    {
        log("Callback " + callback_id + " tick (data=" + data_index + ")");
    
        // draw something using data_index
        float x = 100 + data_index * 40;
        draw_circle(x, 200, 10, 255,200,100,255, 2.0f, false);
    }
    
    int main()
    {
        // Run callback every 50ms
        int cb = register_callback(on_update, 50, 34);
        log("Registered callback " + cb);
    
        return 1; // keep script running
    }

    void log(const string &in message) // Sends a normal message to the UI log overlay.
    void log_error(const string &in message) // Sends an error-styled message to the UI log overlay.
    void log_console(const string &in) // Appends text to the Debug Console (persistent until cleared).

    log_error("Error Log Example");
    log_console("Current HP : 100");

Copy

    float r = 0.0f;
    
    void animate_cursor(int id, int data_index)
    {
        float x, y;
        get_mouse_pos(x, y);
        
        r += 2.0f;
        
        draw_circle(x, y, 12 + sin(r * 0.1f) * 4,
        255, 100, 50, 255,
        2.0f, false);
    }
    
    int main()
    {
        register_callback(animate_cursor, 1, 0);
        return 1;
    }

# CS2 Extended API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

This API is available in both the Uni API and the CS2 product.

In the CS2 product, all standard Proc API functions are supported **except**:

*   Process referencing by PID/name
    
*   Engine-specific helpers
    
*   Virtual memory allocation (`alloc_vm` / `free_vm`)
    

On CS2 Product, `ref_process()` always returns the **CS2 process only**, so it is used like:

Copy

    local cs2 = ref_process()  -- for CS2 Product only

There is **no memory allocation API** exposed in the CS2 product.

* * *

**🔗** `**process:cs2_get_interface(module_base, name)**`

Resolves a **CreateInterface-style** interface exported by a CS2 module.

Copy

    addr = process:cs2_get_interface(module_base, name)

**Parameters**

*   `module_base` Base address of the module that exports `CreateInterface`, e.g.:
    
    *   `"tier0.dll"`
        
    
    Typically obtained via:
    
    Copy
    
        local base, size = process:get_module("tier0.dll")
    
*   `name` Interface name string, e.g.:
    
    *   `"VEngineCvar007"`
        
    

**Returns**

*   Absolute pointer to the resolved interface (Lua integer).
    
*   `0` if the interface cannot be found or the arguments are invalid.
    

* * *

**🧬** `**process:cs2_get_schema_dump()**`

Dumps all Schema System fields for `client.dll` via `schemasystem.dll`.

**Return value**

A **Lua array-style table** (`1..N`) where each element is a table:

**Fields**

*   `name` — `"ClassName::fieldName"`, UTF-8 string e.g. `"CPulse_CallInfo::m_nEditorNodeID"`, `"C_BaseEntity::m_iHealth"`
    
*   `offset` — field offset from the base of that class.
    

If no schema data can be read, returns an **empty table**.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/cs2-extended-api#example-interface-lookup--schema-dump-lua)

🧪 Example – Interface Lookup + Schema Dump (Lua)

[PreviousUtilities](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities)
[NextOverview](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/overview)

Last updated 13 days ago

Copy

    entries = process:cs2_get_schema_dump()

Copy

    {
        name   = "ClassName::fieldName", -- string
        offset = 0x10,                   -- integer offset
    }

Copy

    local function dump_schema(proc)
        local entries = proc:cs2_get_schema_dump()
        if not entries or #entries == 0 then
            log("[LUA] schema dump empty")
            return
        end
    
        log("[LUA] Dumping " .. #entries .. " schema fields...")
    
        for i = 1, #entries do
            local e = entries[i]
            if e then
                -- format: CPulse_CallInfo::m_nEditorNodeID @ 0x00000010
                log(string.format(
                    "%s @ 0x%08X",
                    e.name,
                    e.offset
                ))
            end
        end
    
        log("[LUA] Schema dump complete.")
    end
    
    function main()
        -- Uni API build:
        local cs2 = ref_process("cs2.exe")
    
        -- On the CS2 Product build, just use:
        --   local cs2 = ref_process()
    
        if not cs2 or not cs2:alive() then
            log("[LUA] cs2.exe not found")
            return 0
        end
    
        local tierBase, tierSize = cs2:get_module("tier0.dll")
        if not tierBase then
            log("[LUA] tier0.dll not found")
            return 0
        end
    
        local iface = cs2:cs2_get_interface(tierBase, "VEngineCvar007")
        if iface == 0 then
            log("[LUA] interface not found!")
            return 0
        end
    
        log(string.format(
            "VEngineCvar007 interface at 0x%016X",
            iface
        ))
    
        dump_schema(cs2)
        return 1
    end

# Overview | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

This environment provides a lightweight scripting layer for UI, rendering, memory analysis and interaction in Perception.cx. It uses **AngelScript** with core add-ons and PCX-specific APIs enabled by default.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/overview#core-add-ons)

Core Add-ons

The following standard AngelScript modules are registered:

*   **string** — native string support.
    
*   **array** — dynamic arrays with value semantics.
    
*   **dictionary** — key/value associative maps.
    
*   **math** — standard math utilities.
    
*   **any** — variant type for mixed data.
    
*   **grid** — 2D grid storage type.
    
*   **script helper** — Exception helper functions
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/overview#pcx-addons)

PCX Addons

Custom host APIs extend the scripting environment:

*   **Render API** — draw shapes, text, images, and gradients
    
*   **Input API** — mouse, keyboard, and scroll input
    
*   **Host Utilities** — logging and script lifecycle helpers
    
*   **Proc API** — memory inspection and manipulation
    
*   **Mutex API** — thread-safety primitives for synchronized access
    
*   **GUI API** — create and interact with UI elements
    
*   **System API** — CPU info, instruction utilities, disassembly
    
*   **Net API** — HTTP, HTTPS, and WebSocket networking
    
*   **File System API** — read, write, and manage files/folders
    
*   **Extended Math API** — vectors, matrices, quaternions, and math helpers
    
*   **Engine Specific API** — read engine specific structures easier
    
*   **Json API**
    
*   **Utilities** — encoding, decoding, etc
    
*   **Bit Reinterpret Helpers** — convert values by reinterpreting their underlying bit patterns
    
*   **CS2 Extended API** \- For Official CS2 Product
    

[PreviousCS2 Extended API](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/cs2-extended-api)
[NextLife Cycle](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle)

Last updated 11 days ago

*   [Core Add-ons](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/overview#core-add-ons)
    
*   [PCX Addons](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/overview#pcx-addons)

# Mutex API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The Mutex API provides lightweight thread synchronization inside AngelScript. Mutex objects are native engine primitives exposed as `mutex_t` handles. They support:

*   **Exclusive locks (writers)**
    
*   **Shared locks (readers)**
    
*   **Non-blocking try-lock operations**
    
*   **Automatic cleanup on script shutdown**
    

Mutexes are created by `create_mutex()` and manually released using `destroy()`

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#creating-mutexes)

🔑 Creating Mutexes

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#create)

Create

Copy

    mutex_t create_mutex();

Creates a new mutex and registers it with the current AngelScript context.

Example:

Copy

    mutex_t m = create_mutex();

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#destroy)

Destroy

Copy

    void mutex_t::destroy();

Frees the underlying native mutex.

> **Note:** If the script forgets to call `destroy()`, the PCX engine frees all remaining mutexes when the script context unloads.

Example:

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#exclusive-lock-writer-lock)

🔐 Exclusive Lock (Writer Lock)

Use these when only one thread should modify shared state.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#lock-blocking)

Lock (blocking)

Blocks until exclusive ownership is acquired.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#try-lock-non-blocking)

Try Lock (non-blocking)

Returns `true` if the lock is acquired immediately, `false` otherwise.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#unlock)

Unlock

Releases the exclusive lock.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#shared-lock-reader-lock)

📖 Shared Lock (Reader Lock)

Shared locks allow **multiple readers**, but automatically block if an exclusive writer holds the lock.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#lock-shared-blocking)

Lock Shared (blocking)

Blocks until a shared lock is available.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#try-lock-shared-non-blocking)

Try Lock Shared (non-blocking)

Returns immediately with `true` on success.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#unlock-shared)

Unlock Shared

Releases the shared lock.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#usage-example)

🧩 Usage Example

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#automatic-cleanup)

🗑 Automatic Cleanup

Even if a script forgets:

PCX will:

*   Free each `mtx_t` safely
    
*   Avoid leaks and invalid handles
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#avoid-deadlocks)

Avoid Deadlocks!

*   You must avoid deadlocks
    
*   If an exception happens and the active thread had a lock, It will cause a deadlock
    
*   Use the following try & catch logic to avoid it.
    

[PreviousProc API](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/proc-api)
[NextGUI API](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/gui-api)

Last updated 22 days ago

*   [🔑 Creating Mutexes](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#creating-mutexes)
    
*   [🔐 Exclusive Lock (Writer Lock)](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#exclusive-lock-writer-lock)
    
*   [📖 Shared Lock (Reader Lock)](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#shared-lock-reader-lock)
    
*   [🧩 Usage Example](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#usage-example)
    
*   [🗑 Automatic Cleanup](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#automatic-cleanup)
    
*   [Avoid Deadlocks!](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/mutex-api#avoid-deadlocks)
    

Copy

    m.destroy();

Copy

    void mutex_t::lock();

Copy

    bool mutex_t::try_lock();

Copy

    void mutex_t::unlock();

Copy

    void mutex_t::lock_shared();

Copy

    bool mutex_t::try_lock_shared();

Copy

    void mutex_t::unlock_shared();

Copy

    mutex_t g_mtx = create_mutex();
    
    int sharedValue = 0;
    
    void writer_thread(int callback_id, int data_index)
    {
        g_mtx.lock();
        log("[writer] acquired exclusive lock");
        
        sharedValue += 10;
        
        g_mtx.unlock();
        log("[writer] released lock");
    }
    
    void reader_thread(int callback_id, int data_index)
    {
        if (g_mtx.try_lock_shared())
        {
            log("[reader] acquired shared lock");
            int v = sharedValue;  // safe read
            g_mtx.unlock_shared();
            log("[reader] released shared lock");
        }
        else
        {
            log("[reader] shared lock unavailable");
        }
    }
    
    int main()
    {
        
        register_callback(writer_thread, 1, 0);
        register_callback(reader_thread, 1, 0);
        return 1;
    }
    
    void on_unload()
    {
        log("unloaded");
        // Optional: manual cleanup
        g_mtx.destroy();
    }
    

Copy

    mutex_t m = create_mutex();
    // ... never calls m.destroy()

Copy

    mutex_t g_example_mutex;
    
    // A safe function that guarantees the mutex is always unlocked.
    void do_work_safe(bool should_throw)
    {
        log("Attempting to lock the mutex...");
        g_example_mutex.lock();
        log("Mutex locked.");
    
        try
        {
            if (should_throw)
            {
                log("An error occurred! Throwing an exception...");
                throw("Error");
            }
        }
        catch
        {
            log("Caught an exception, but the unlock call will still be reached.");
        }
    
        // This code is now guaranteed to run, preventing a deadlock.
        g_example_mutex.unlock();
        log("Mutex unlocked.");
    }
    
    void main()
    {
        g_example_mutex = create_mutex();
    
        // 1. Call the function and make it throw an exception.
        //    The function will catch its own exception and unlock the mutex.
        do_work_safe(true);
        
        // 2. Call it again. This will now succeed because the mutex was released.
        log("Calling the function again. This will work correctly.");
        do_work_safe(false);
    
        log("Program finished successfully.");
    }

---

# Json API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The JSON API provides simple, fast parsing and encoding of JSON using native Lua data types. All JSON features are exposed under the global `json` table.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#overview)

Overview

The `json` module supports:

Operation

Description

`**json.parse(str)**`

Parse a JSON string into Lua values

`**json.decode(str)**`

Alias of `json.parse`

`**json.stringify(value)**`

Convert Lua values into JSON

`**json.encode(value)**`

Alias of `json.stringify`

The API is intentionally minimal and strictly uses plain Lua tables, numbers, booleans, strings, and `nil`.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#json-lua-json.parse-json.decode)

JSON → Lua: `json.parse` / `json.decode`

Copy

    value, err = json.parse(string)
    value, err = json.decode(string)

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#parameters)

Parameters

*   **string** — a UTF-8 JSON text.
    

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#returns)

Returns

*   On success: **Lua value representing the JSON structure**
    
*   On error: `nil, "error message"`
    

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#lua-type-mapping)

Lua Type Mapping

JSON

Lua

Object `{}`

Table `{ key = value }`

Array `[]`

Table `{ [1] = ..., [2] = ... }`

`"text"`

string

`123`

number

`true` / `false`

boolean

`null`

`**nil**` (field disappears when iterating!)

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#example)

Example

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#invalid-json-example)

Invalid JSON example

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#lua-json-json.stringify-json.encode)

Lua → JSON: `json.stringify` / `json.encode`

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#parameters-1)

Parameters

*   **value** — any Lua value (table / string / number / boolean / nil)
    

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#returns-1)

Returns

*   On success: **string containing JSON**
    
*   On failure: `nil, "error message"`
    

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#supported-lua-types)

Supported Lua Types

Lua

JSON

String

`"text"`

Number

`123` or `1.23`

Boolean

`true` / `false`

Table

Object or Array _(auto-detected)_

nil

`null` _(inside tables only)_

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#array-vs-object-detection)

Array vs Object Detection

Lua tables are encoded as JSON arrays **only** if they contain:

*   continuous integer keys
    
*   starting from `1`
    
*   with no gaps
    

Otherwise they become JSON objects.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#example-1)

Example

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#mixed-tables)

Mixed Tables

Tables with both numeric and string keys become JSON objects:

Round-Trip Example

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#null-handling)

Null Handling

JSON `null` becomes **Lua** `**nil**`.

This means fields may “disappear” from tables:

This is correct behavior and matches typical JSON–Lua conventions.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#error-handling)

Error Handling

All functions safely return:

Examples of failure:

*   malformed JSON
    
*   unsupported Lua type (function, userdata, thread)
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#summary)

Function

Description

`json.decode(str)`

Alias of parse

`json.stringify(val)`

Encode Lua value into JSON

Alias of stringify

Copy

    local data, err = json.parse('{"a":1,"b":[10,20],"flag":true}')
    print(data.a)         --> 1
    print(data.b[1])      --> 10
    print(data.flag)      --> true

Copy

    local v, e = json.parse("{ broken json }")
    if not v then
        print("Parse failed:", e)
    end

Copy

    json_str, err = json.stringify(value)
    json_str, err = json.encode(value)

Copy

    local obj = {
        hello = "world",
        numbers = { 1, 2, 3 }
    }
    
    local json_str = json.stringify(obj)
    print(json_str)
    -- {"hello":"world","numbers":[1,2,3]}

Copy

    local t = { [1] = "first", [3] = "third", foo = "bar" }
    print(json.stringify(t))
    -- {"3":"third","1":"first","foo":"bar"}

Copy

    local original = {
        text = "hello",
        list = { 10, 20, 30 },
        nested = { a = 1, b = { "x", "y" } }
    }
    
    local encoded = json.stringify(original)
    local decoded = json.parse(encoded)
    
    -- decoded now matches `original`

Copy

    local obj = json.parse('{"a":1,"b":null,"c":2}')
    -- obj = { a = 1, c = 2 }

Copy

    nil, "error message"
