# Engine Specific API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#unreal-engine-helpers-unreal_engine)

Unreal Engine Helpers (`unreal_engine`)

The `unreal_engine` table contains helpers for working with Unreal Engine games (UE4 / UE5).

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#unreal_engine.read_tarray)

`unreal_engine.read_tarray`

Copy

    unreal_engine.read_tarray(proc, tarray_address[, max_count]) -> table

Reads an Unreal-style dynamic array (`TArray`) and returns its contents as a Lua array of pointers.

**Parameters**

*   `proc` Process object used for reading game memory.
    
*   `tarray_address` Integer address of the array in game memory.
    
*   `max_count` _(optional, default: 4096)_ Maximum number of elements to read. Used as a safety limit.
    

**Returns**

*   A Lua array table indexed from `1` upward, containing integer addresses (pointers).
    
*   If anything is invalid (bad address, null pointer, weird count), an **empty table** is returned.
    

**Example**

Copy

    local actors = unreal_engine.read_tarray(proc, actors_array_addr, 1024)
    
    for i, actor_ptr in ipairs(actors) do
        -- actor_ptr is an integer address inside the game
    end

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info)

`unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info`

Reads a camera/view structure and converts it into a normalized Lua table.

**Parameters**

*   `proc` Process object.
    
*   `view_info_address` Address of the camera/view information in memory.
    

**Returns**

A table with this structure:

If the address or process is invalid, an **empty table** is returned.

**Example**

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info_f64)

`unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info_f64`

Same purpose as `read_minimal_view_info`, but for layouts that use **double-precision** values (common in some UE5 setups).

**Parameters**

*   `proc` Process object.
    
*   `view_info_address` Address of the camera/view information in memory.
    

**Returns**

Same shape as the float version:

If inputs are invalid, returns an **empty table**.

**Example**

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#unreal_engine.world_to_screen)

`unreal_engine.world_to_screen`

Projects a point from world space to screen space using camera data.

**Parameters**

*   `world_position` Can be either:
    
    *   A table: `{ x = number, y = number, z = number }`, or
        
    *   Three numbers: `x, y, z`
        
    
*   `view_info` The camera table returned from:
    
    *   `unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info`, or
        
    *   `unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info_f64`
        
    
    Must contain:
    

**Returns**

*   On success (point is in front of the camera):
    
*   If the point is behind the camera: `nil`.
    
*   If input is invalid: a Lua error is raised.
    

**Example**

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#source-2-helpers-source2)

Source 2 Helpers (`source2`)

The `source2` table contains helpers for working with Source 2 games.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#source2.world_to_screen)

`source2.world_to_screen`

Projects a world-space point using a 4×4 **row-major** view-projection matrix.

**Parameters**

*   `world_position` Either:
    
    *   Table `{ x = number, y = number, z = number }`, or
        
    *   Three numbers: `x, y, z`
        
    
*   `view_matrix16` A Lua array with 16 numeric values:
    
    The matrix should be the combined view-projection matrix for the current camera.
    

**Returns**

*   On success:
    
*   If the point is behind the camera: `nil`.
    
*   If `view_matrix16` does not contain at least 16 numbers: a Lua error is raised.
    

**Example**

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#fortnite-helper)

Fortnite Helper

A small helper for reading player names in Fortnite.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#fortnite_get_player_name)

`fortnite_get_player_name`

Attempts to read and decode a player name from game memory.

**Parameters**

*   `proc` Process object.
    
*   `address` Address pointing to a name-related structure in Fortnite.
    

**Returns**

*   The player name as a string on success.
    
*   An empty string `""` if:
    
    *   The process is invalid,
        
    *   The memory cannot be read safely,
        
    *   The decoded name is empty.
        
    

**Example**

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#rust-helper)

Rust Helper

A helper for getting world-space transform positions in Rust (Unity).

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#rust_get_transform_position)

`rust_get_transform_position`

Resolves the world-space position of a Unity transform hierarchy used by Rust.

**Parameters**

*   `proc` Process object.
    
*   `address` Address of a transform-related structure for a given entity.
    

**Returns**

*   On success: three numbers `x, y, z` (Lua returns them as multiple values).
    
*   On failure (invalid process, invalid address, or any internal error): `0, 0, 0`.
    

**Example**

    if x ~= 0 or y ~= 0 or z ~= 0 then
        local screen = unreal_engine.world_to_screen({ x = x, y = y, z = z }, view_info)
        if screen and screen.visible then
            -- draw marker on that entity
        end
    end

# Win API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

This API exposes a small subset of the Win32 window, clipboard, keyboard, mouse and messaging functions to Lua:

*   Work with windows via **handles** (`hwnd` as integer).
    
*   Inspect window rectangles and sizes.
    
*   Check if a window is foreground or “active”.
    
*   Read / write text to the **clipboard** (UTF-8).
    
*   Look up the **thread & process IDs** for a window.
    
*   Send **messages**, **keys**, and **characters** to a window.
    
*   Send **global keyboard and mouse input** via `SendInput`.
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#window-lookup-and-info)

Window Lookup & Info

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#find_window-title-class-greater-than-hwnd-or-nil)

`find_window(title [, class]) -> hwnd | nil`

Search for a top-level window.

*   `title` — window title to match (UTF-8 string).
    
*   `class` — optional window class name (UTF-8 string).
    

If both are provided, both must match. Returns `hwnd` (integer) or `nil` if not found.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#get_window_size-hwnd-greater-than-width-height-or-nil-nil)

`get_window_size(hwnd) -> width, height | nil, nil`

Get the window’s **outer** size in pixels.

*   `hwnd` — window handle (integer).
    

Returns:

*   `width`, `height` (integers), or
    
*   `nil, nil` if the handle is invalid or the call fails.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#get_window_rect-hwnd-greater-than-x-y-width-height-or-nil-nil-nil-nil)

`get_window_rect(hwnd) -> x, y, width, height | nil, nil, nil, nil`

Get the window’s full rectangle in screen coordinates.

*   `x`, `y` — top-left screen coordinates.
    
*   `width`, `height` — size in pixels.
    

Returns all `nil` on failure.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#window-focus-and-activity)

Window Focus & Activity

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#is_foreground_window-hwnd-greater-than-bool)

`is_foreground_window(hwnd) -> bool`

Checks if `hwnd` is the **current foreground window**.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#is_window_active-hwnd-greater-than-bool)

`is_window_active(hwnd) -> bool`

Checks if a window is “active” in a broad sense:

*   is a valid window,
    
*   is visible,
    
*   is **not minimized**.
    

Returns `true` or `false`.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#window-text-and-class)

Window Text & Class

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#get_window_title-hwnd-greater-than-string-or-nil)

`get_window_title(hwnd) -> string | nil`

Get the window’s title as a UTF-8 string.

*   Returns `""` for empty titles.
    
*   Returns `nil` if the handle is invalid.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#get_window_class-hwnd-greater-than-string-or-nil)

`get_window_class(hwnd) -> string | nil`

Get the window’s **class name**.

*   Returns `""` if class name can’t be read.
    
*   Returns `nil` if the handle is invalid.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#set_foreground_window-hwnd-greater-than-bool)

`set_foreground_window(hwnd) -> bool`

Attempts to bring the given window to the foreground.

Returns `true` on success, `false` otherwise.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#clipboard)

Clipboard

All clipboard operations use UTF-8 strings.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#copy_to_clipboard-text-greater-than-bool)

`copy_to_clipboard(text) -> bool`

Copies a Lua string into the system clipboard.

*   `text` — UTF-8 string.
    
*   Returns `true` on success, `false` on failure.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#copy_from_clipboard-greater-than-string)

`copy_from_clipboard() -> string`

Reads UTF-8 text from the system clipboard.

*   Returns `""` (empty string) if:
    
    *   clipboard cannot be opened,
        
    *   the clipboard doesn’t contain text, or
        
    *   any error occurs.
        
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#thread-process-info)

Thread / Process Info

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#get_window_thread_process_id-hwnd-greater-than-thread_id-process_id-or-nil-nil)

`get_window_thread_process_id(hwnd) -> thread_id, process_id | nil, nil`

Returns IDs associated with a given window.

*   `thread_id` — thread that owns the window.
    
*   `process_id` — process that owns the thread.
    

If the handle is invalid or the IDs can’t be obtained, returns `nil, nil`.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#messages-and-keys)

Messages & Keys

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#post_message-hwnd-msg-wparam-lparam-greater-than-bool)

`post_message(hwnd, msg, wparam, lparam) -> bool`

Low-level API to post a message to a window.

*   `hwnd` — window handle.
    
*   `msg` — message ID (e.g., `0x0010` for `WM_CLOSE`).
    
*   `wparam`, `lparam` — integer parameters.
    

Returns `true` on success.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#global-key-input-sendinput)

Global key input (`SendInput`)

These functions send **global** keyboard input (not scoped to a specific window). Use when you simply want to simulate key presses.

Virtual keys are integers (e.g. `0x41` for `A`, `0x11` for Ctrl, `0x0D` for Enter).

`**win_key_down(vk)**`

Simulate key down for virtual key `vk`.

`**win_key_up(vk)**`

Simulate key up for virtual key `vk`.

`**win_key_press(vk [, delay_ms])**`

Press and release a key, with an optional delay.

*   `vk` — virtual key code.
    
*   `delay_ms` — optional delay in milliseconds between down and up (default ~30, clamped to `0..1000`).
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#message-based-character-and-key-sending)

Message-based character & key sending

These functions target a specific window using messages (`WM_CHAR`, `WM_KEYDOWN`, `WM_KEYUP`).

`**send_char(hwnd, text) -> bool**`

Sends a single character via `WM_CHAR`.

*   `text` — Lua string; only the **first UTF-16 code unit** is used, which is fine for most BMP characters.
    

Returns `true` on success.

`**send_key(hwnd, vk) -> bool**`

Sends a key to a specific window using `WM_KEYDOWN` and `WM_KEYUP`.

*   `vk` — virtual key code.
    

Returns `true` if both messages were posted successfully.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#mouse-input)

Mouse Input

All mouse functions send **global** input via `SendInput`.

Coordinates are in **screen pixels** (primary monitor), unless noted otherwise.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#mouse_move-x-y)

`mouse_move(x, y)`

Moves the cursor to absolute screen coordinates.

*   `(0,0)` is top-left of the primary display.
    
*   Coordinates are converted to the normalized range expected by `SendInput`.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#mouse_move_relative-dx-dy)

`mouse_move_relative(dx, dy)`

Moves the cursor relative to its current position.

*   `dx` — horizontal delta (pixels).
    
*   `dy` — vertical delta (pixels).
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#mouse_left_click)

`mouse_left_click()`

Performs a left button click at the current cursor position.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#mouse_right_click)

`mouse_right_click()`

Performs a right button click.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#mouse_middle_click)

`mouse_middle_click()`

Performs a middle button click.

Each click sends a down event, waits ~10 ms, then sends an up event.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#mouse_scroll-amount)

`mouse_scroll(amount)`

Scrolls the mouse wheel vertically.

*   `amount` is in “notches”:
    
    *   positive → scroll **up**
        
    *   negative → scroll **down**
        
    

Example: `mouse_scroll(3)` scrolls up 3 notches.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api#util)

**Util**


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`get_tickcount64()`

*   GetTickCount64()

    local title   = "Untitled - Notepad"
    local hwnd    = find_window(title)
    
    if not hwnd then
      print("Window not found:", title)
      return
    end
    
    print("HWND:", string.format("0x%X", hwnd))
    
    local x, y, w, h = get_window_rect(hwnd)
    print("Rect:", x, y, w, h)
    
    local winTitle = get_window_title(hwnd) or "<nil>"
    local winClass = get_window_class(hwnd) or "<nil>"
    print("Title:", winTitle)
    print("Class:", winClass)
    
    local tid, pid = get_window_thread_process_id(hwnd)
    print("Thread ID:", tid, "Process ID:", pid)

    -- Type 'HELLO'
    local letters = { 0x48, 0x45, 0x4C, 0x4C, 0x4F } -- H E L L O
    for _, vk in ipairs(letters) do
      win_key_press(vk, 40)
    end

    local VK_CONTROL = 0x11
    local VK_V       = 0x56

    win_key_up(VK_CONTROL)

Copy

    local hwnd = find_window("Untitled - Notepad")
    if not hwnd then return end
    
    -- make sure Notepad has focus (if you expose set_foreground_window)
    set_foreground_window(hwnd)
    
    send_char(hwnd, "H")
    send_char(hwnd, "i")
    send_char(hwnd, " ")
    send_char(hwnd, "🌸")
    
    local VK_RETURN = 0x0D
    send_key(hwnd, VK_RETURN)

Copy

    -- Move to near top-left, left-click
    mouse_move(100, 100)
    mouse_left_click()
    
    -- Move a bit to the right and right-click
    mouse_move_relative(80, 0)
    mouse_right_click()
    
    -- Move down and middle-click
    mouse_move_relative(0, 60)
    mouse_middle_click()
    
    -- Scroll up then down
    mouse_scroll(3)
    mouse_scroll(-3)

Copy

    local TARGET_TITLE = "Untitled - Notepad"  -- change to your target window
    
    local function has_global(name)
        return _G[name] ~= nil
    end
    
    local function get_target_hwnd()
        if not has_global("find_window") then
            log("ERROR: find_window is not available.")
            return nil
        end
    
        local hwnd = find_window(TARGET_TITLE)
        if not hwnd then
            log("Window not found:", TARGET_TITLE)
            return nil
        end
    
        log("Found hwnd:", string.format("0x%X", hwnd))
    
        if has_global("set_foreground_window") then
            local ok = set_foreground_window(hwnd)
            log("set_foreground_window:", ok)
        else
            log("set_foreground_window not available, skipping.")
        end
    
        return hwnd
    end
    
    local function test_mouse_basic()
        log("=== TEST: mouse movement & clicks ===")
        log("Move your eyes to where the cursor goes. :)")
    
        -- Move to approximate top-left of the primary screen
        mouse_move(100, 100)
        mouse_left_click()
        log("  mouse_move(100,100) + left click")
    
        -- Move a bit to the right and right-click
        mouse_move_relative(80, 0)
        mouse_right_click()
        log("  mouse_move_relative(80,0) + right click")
    
        -- Move a bit down and middle-click
        mouse_move_relative(0, 60)
        mouse_middle_click()
        log("  mouse_move_relative(0,60) + middle click")
    
        -- Scroll up then down a bit
        mouse_scroll(3)   -- up 3 notches
        mouse_scroll(-3)  -- down 3 notches
        log("  mouse_scroll(3) then mouse_scroll(-3)")
    end
    
    local function test_send_char_key(hwnd)
        if not hwnd then
            log("No hwnd, skipping send_char/send_key test.")
            return
        end
    
        if not has_global("send_char") or not has_global("send_key") then
            log("send_char / send_key not available, skipping.")
            return
        end
    
        log("=== TEST: send_char / send_key ===")
        log("Make sure the target window has a focused text field.")
    
        -- Send "Hi " + emoji via WM_CHAR
        send_char(hwnd, "H")
        send_char(hwnd, "i")
        send_char(hwnd, " ")
        send_char(hwnd, "🌸") -- only 
    
        -- Press Enter via WM_KEYDOWN/UP
        local VK_RETURN = 0x0D
        local ok = send_key(hwnd, VK_RETURN)
        log("send_key(VK_RETURN) ->", ok)
    end
    
    function main()
        log("Target window title:", TARGET_TITLE)
    
        local hwnd = get_target_hwnd()
    
        test_mouse_basic()
        test_send_char_key(hwnd)
    
        log("=== winapi_input_test.lua done ===")
        return 1;
    end

# Life Cycle | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#script-lifecycle-and-entry-point)

🧠 Script Lifecycle & Entry Point


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Every AngelScript module loaded by the PCX engine **must define** an entry function:

The engine automatically looks up and executes this function when the script is started.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#load-event)

Load Event

Copy

    int main()

Return Value

Meaning

\> 0

Keep the script **loaded and active**. Callbacks, draw events, and per-frame updates continue to run.

<= 0

**Unload** the script immediately after `main()` completes. All registered callbacks and allocated resources are released.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#unload-event)

Unload Event

Copy

    void on_unload()

*   Called once **when the script is about to be unloaded**.
    
*   Use this to clean up state, save data, etc.
    
*   Cannot prevent the script from unloading
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#execution-flow)

🔹 Execution Flow

1.  When a script is loaded, the engine locates and runs its `main()` function.
    
2.  Inside `main()`, you typically register callbacks or set up states.
    
3.  After `main()` returns:
    
    *   If the return value > 0 → the script remains active (engine thread persists).
        
    *   If the return value ≤ 0 → the script is unloaded, memory is freed, and its callbacks are destroyed.
        
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#example-1-persistent-script)

🔹 Example #1 — Persistent Script

The engine will keep this script alive until it’s explicitly unloaded.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#example-2-one-shot-script)

🔹 Example #2 — One-shot Script

After this executes, the script and its thread context are released.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#engine-integration-notes)

🔹 Engine Integration Notes

*   The engine checks the return value of `main()` immediately after execution.
    
*   Scripts with `main() > 0` are marked as _persistent_ and remain loaded in the module table.
    
*   Scripts returning `0` or negative values are **unloaded** and their memory is freed.
    
*   `unregister_callback(id)` can be called at any time to stop background threads gracefully.
    
*   `main` should never have any infinite loops.
    

[PreviousOverview](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/overview)
[NextEngine](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine)

Last updated 25 days ago

*   [🧠 Script Lifecycle & Entry Point](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#script-lifecycle-and-entry-point)
    
*   [Load Event](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#load-event)
    
*   [Unload Event](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#unload-event)
    
*   [🔹 Execution Flow](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#execution-flow)
    
*   [🔹 Example #1 — Persistent Script](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#example-1-persistent-script)
    
*   [🔹 Example #2 — One-shot Script](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#example-2-one-shot-script)
    
*   [🔹 Engine Integration Notes](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/life-cycle#engine-integration-notes)
    

Copy

    void on_tick(int id, int data_index)
    {
        float vw, vh; get_view(vw, vh);
        float cx = vw * 0.5f, cy = vh * 0.5f;
    
        uint64 font = get_font20();
    
        draw_rect_filled(cx - 100, cy - 50, 200, 100,
                         40, 40, 40, 255, 8.0f, RR_TOP_LEFT|RR_TOP_RIGHT);
    
        draw_text("Hello World", cx - 60, cy - 10,
                  255,255,255,255, font, TE_SHADOW,
                  0,0,0,180, 1.0f, true);
    }
    
    int main()
    {
         log("Starting persistent script...");
    
        // Run every 16 ms (~60 FPS)
        register_callback(on_tick, 16 , 0);
    
        // Stay loaded indefinitely
        return 1;
    }
    
    void on_unload()
    {
         log("Unloaded script...");
    }

Copy

    int main()
    {
        log("One-shot initialization...");
        // Return 0 to indicate we’re done — unload immediately
        return 0;
    }

# System API (CPU & Disassembly) | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The **System API** provides low-level functionality for CPU information, performance timing, and x64 instruction disassembly using **Zydis**. All functions listed here are available globally inside Lua scripts.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#available-functions)

📌 **Available Functions**

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#cpu-information)

**CPU Information**

Function

Returns

Description

`cpu_vendor()`

`string`

CPU vendor (e.g. `"AuthenticAMD"` or `"GenuineIntel"`).

`cpu_brand()`

`string`

Human-readable CPU model string.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#timing-functions)

**Timing Functions**

Function

Returns

Description

`rdtsc()`

`uint64`

Raw timestamp counter from the CPU. Fast but CPU-frequency dependent.

`perf_time()`

`int64`

High-resolution performance counter ticks from Windows.

`perf_frequency()`

`int64`

Number of performance counter ticks per second.

Useful for accurate microbenchmarking:

Copy

    seconds = (perf_time_end - perf_time_start) / perf_frequency()

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#disassembly-zydis)

**Disassembly (Zydis)**

Function

Returns

Description

`zydis_disasm(bytes_table, [runtime_rip])`

`table` (array of instructions)

Disassembles multiple x64 instructions and returns detailed structured output.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#instruction-structure)

**Instruction Structure**


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`zydis_disasm` returns an **array of** `**disasm_instruction_t**`. Each instruction contains:

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#operand-structure)

**Operand Structure**


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Each operand is an `operand_t` table with a consistent schema:

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#usage-examples)

Copy

    {
        runtime_address       = 0x140000000,  -- uint64
        length                = 5,            -- bytes
        mnemonic              = "mov",        -- "push", "call", etc.
        text                  = "mov rbp, rsp",  -- full Intel syntax
        operand_count         = 3,            -- total (explicit + hidden)
        operand_count_visible = 2,            -- explicit operands only
    
        operands = { operand_t, operand_t, ... }
    }

Copy

    {
        id         = 0,
        visibility = "explicit", -- "explicit" | "implicit" | "hidden"
        type       = "reg",      -- "reg" | "mem" | "imm" | "ptr" | "unused"
        size       = 64,         -- bits
    
        -- Register operand
        reg = {
            name = "rbp"
        },
    
        -- Memory operand
        mem = {
            segment          = "ss",
            base             = "rsp",
            index            = nil,
            scale            = 1,
            has_displacement = true,
            displacement     = -0x20,
        },
    
        -- Immediate operand
        imm = {
            is_signed        = true,
            is_relative      = false,
            value            = 48,
            absolute_address = nil, -- if relative & resolvable
        },
    
        -- Pointer operand
        ptr = {
            segment = 0x1234,
            offset  = 0xABCDEF,
        }
    }

Copy

    function main()
        log("CPU Vendor: " .. cpu_vendor())
        log("CPU Brand : " .. cpu_brand())
    end

Copy

    function main()
        local freq = perf_frequency()
        local t0 = perf_time()
    
        -- workload
        for i = 1, 1000000 do end
    
        local t1 = perf_time()
    
        local dt = (t1 - t0) / freq
        log("Elapsed seconds: " .. dt)
    end

Copy

    function main()
        local bytes = {
            0x55,                    -- push rbp
            0x48, 0x89, 0xE5,        -- mov rbp, rsp
            0x48, 0x83, 0xEC, 0x30   -- sub rsp, 0x30
        }
    
        local ins = zydis_disasm(bytes, 0x140000000)
    
        for i, inst in ipairs(ins) do
            log(string.format("0x%X: %s", inst.runtime_address, inst.text))
        end
    end

Copy

    function main()
        local p = ref_process("notepad.exe")
        if not p then return end
    
        local base = p:base_address()
        local bytes = p:rvm(base, 32)
    
        local ins = zydis_disasm(bytes, base)
    
        for _, inst in ipairs(ins) do
            log(inst.runtime_address .. ": " .. inst.text)
        end
    
        deref_process(p)
    end

Copy

    0x140000000: push rbp
      mnemonic = push, length = 1, operands = 1/3
        op1: id=0 type=reg vis=explicit size=64
          reg: rbp
        op2: id=1 type=reg vis=hidden size=64
          reg: rsp
        op3: id=2 type=mem vis=hidden size=64
          mem: seg=ss base=rsp index=nil scale=0 has_disp=false disp=nil
    
    0x140000001: mov rbp, rsp
      mnemonic = mov, length = 3, operands = 2/2
    
    0x140000004: sub rsp, 0x30
      mnemonic = sub, length = 4, operands = 2/3

Copy

    local dt = get_datetime()
    -- dt = {
    --     year        = 2025,
    --     month       = 11,
    --     day         = 27,
    --     hour        = 14,        -- 24h clock
    --     minute      = 5,
    --     second      = 33,
    --     msec        = 120,
    --
    --     day_name    = "Thursday",
    --     month_name  = "November",
    --
    --     hour12      = 2,         -- 12h clock
    --     ampm        = "PM"
    -- }

Copy

    local ts = get_timestamp()
    -- example: 1732734005

Copy

    function main()
        local dt = get_datetime()
    
        log(string.format(
            "Today is %s, %s %d, %d",
            dt.day_name, dt.month_name, dt.day, dt.year
        ))
    
        log(string.format(
            "Local Time: %d:%02d %s",
            dt.hour12, dt.minute, dt.ampm
        ))
    
        local ts = get_timestamp()
        log("Unix Timestamp: " .. ts)
    end

# Engine Specific API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine-specific-api#unreal-engine-helpers)

Unreal Engine Helpers

The following helpers are designed for Unreal Engine–based games (UE4 & UE5), including both float-precision and double-precision view structures.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine-specific-api#bool-unreal_read_tarray-proc_t-and-in-proc-uint64-tarray_addr-array-less-than-uint64-greater-than-an)

`bool unreal_read_tarray(proc_t &in proc, uint64 tarray_addr, array<uint64> &out result, uint max_count = 4096)`

Reads an Unreal `TArray` from memory and fills a script array with the pointer values inside it.

**Parameters**

*   **proc** — target process handle
    
*   **tarray\_addr** — memory address of the `TArray`
    
*   **result** — output array that will receive the entries
    
*   **max\_count** — safety limit for max number of elements (default 4096)
    

**Returns**

`true` on success, `false` on invalid address, invalid process, or corrupted data.

On failure, `result` will be empty.

**Example**

Copy

    array<uint64> actors;
    if (unreal_read_tarray(proc, actors_addr, actors))
    {
        for (uint i = 0; i < actors.length(); i++)
            log("Actor pointer: " + actors[i]);
    }

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine-specific-api#bool-unreal_read_minimal_view_info-proc_t-and-in-proc-uint64-pov_addr-vector3-and-out-location-vecto)

`bool unreal_read_minimal_view_info(proc_t &in proc, uint64 pov_addr, vector3 &out location, vector3 &out rotation, double &out fov)`

Reads a **float-precision** Unreal camera view.

**Parameters**

*   **proc** — process handle
    
*   **pov\_addr** — address of camera/view structure
    
*   **location** — output camera world position
    
*   **rotation** — output camera rotation (pitch, yaw, roll)
    
*   **fov** — output field-of-view
    

**Returns**

`true` on success, `false` on invalid input.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine-specific-api#bool-unreal_read_minimal_view_info_f64-proc_t-and-in-proc-uint64-pov_addr-vector3-and-out-location-v)

`bool unreal_read_minimal_view_info_f64(proc_t &in proc, uint64 pov_addr, vector3 &out location, vector3 &out rotation, double &out fov)`

Same as above but for **double-precision** UE5 view structures.

Use this if the game uses large-world coordinates or 64-bit FOV/rotation data.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine-specific-api#bool-unreal_world_to_screen-const-vector3-and-in-world_pos-const-vector3-and-in-cam_location-const-v)

`bool unreal_world_to_screen(const vector3 &in world_pos, const vector3 &in cam_location, const vector3 &in cam_rotation, double fov_deg, vector2 &out screen_pos)`

Projects a 3D world point into 2D screen coordinates using a UE-style camera.

**Parameters**

*   **world\_pos** — world-space position
    
*   **cam\_location** — camera location
    
*   **cam\_rotation** — camera rotation (pitch, yaw, roll)
    
*   **fov\_deg** — vertical field-of-view in degrees
    
*   **screen\_pos** — output pixel coordinate
    

**Returns**

*   `true` if the point is visible, and `screen_pos` is valid
    
*   `false` if the point is behind the camera
    

**Example**

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine-specific-api#source-2-helpers)

Source 2 Helpers

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine-specific-api#bool-source2_world_to_screen-const-vector3-and-in-world_pos-const-matrix4x4-and-in-view_matrix-vecto)

`bool source2_world_to_screen(const vector3 &in world_pos, const matrix4x4 &in view_matrix, vector2 &out screen_pos)`

Projects a world position using a **row-major 4×4 view-projection matrix**.

**Parameters**

*   **world\_pos** — world-space vector
    
*   **view\_matrix** — 16-element row-major view-projection matrix
    
*   **screen\_pos** — output pixel position
    

**Returns**

*   `true` if visible
    
*   `false` if behind the camera
    

**Example**

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine-specific-api#fortnite-helper)

Fortnite Helper

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine-specific-api#string-fortnite_get_player_name-proc_t-and-in-proc-uint64-addr)

`string fortnite_get_player_name(proc_t &in proc, uint64 addr)`

Reads and decrypts a Fortnite player name from memory.

**Returns**

*   Player name on success
    
*   Empty string `""` on failure

`vector3 rust_get_transform_position(proc_t &in proc, uint64 addr)`

Resolves the world-space position of a Rust (Unity) transform hierarchy.

**Returns**

# File System | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

**API Folder Location** : C:\\Users\\"UserName"\\Documents\\My Games\\

Filesystem API that allows scripts to read, write, and manage files **only inside the main scripting directory**.

Scripts **cannot** access, modify, create, or query files **outside** this directory. All paths must be **relative** and are automatically sandboxed for safety.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#overview)

Overview

The filesystem API provides the following capabilities:

*   Create files
    
*   Create directories
    
*   Read files
    
*   Check if a file exists
    
*   List files or directories
    
*   Delete files
    
*   Delete directories
    

All functions are available as **global AngelScript functions**.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#path-rules)

Path Rules

To ensure safety and consistency:

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#paths-must-be-relative)

✔ Paths must be relative

Absolute paths such as:

are not allowed.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#parent-directory-traversal-is-not-allowed)

✔ Parent-directory traversal is not allowed

Paths cannot contain:

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#scripts-cannot-escape-the-main-scripting-directory)

✔ Scripts cannot escape the main scripting directory

Every operation is automatically constrained to the script directory.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#global-functions)

Global Functions

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#bool-create_file-const-string-and-in-path-const-string-and-in-data)

`bool create_file(const string &in path, const string &in data = "")`

Creates or overwrites a file at the given relative path.

*   **path** — relative file path under the main scripting directory
    
*   **data** — optional file contents (defaults to empty)
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#bool-create_directory-const-string-and-in-path)

`bool create_directory(const string &in path)`

Creates a directory (non-recursive).

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#bool-read_file-const-string-and-in-path-string-and-out-data)

`bool read_file(const string &in path, string &out data)`

Reads a file and returns its contents through an output parameter.

*   Returns `true` on success, `false` if the file does not exist or could not be read.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#bool-does_file_exist-const-string-and-in-path)

`bool does_file_exist(const string &in path)`

Checks if a file exists.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#bool-query_directory-const-string-and-in-path)

\`bool query\_directory(const string &in path,

bool include\_dirs, bool include\_files, const array<string> &in extensions, array<string> &out entries)\`

Lists the contents of a directory.

**Parameters**

*   `path` — relative directory path under the main scripting directory
    
*   `include_dirs` — if `true`, include subdirectories in the results
    
*   `include_files` — if `true`, include files in the results
    
*   `extensions` — list of file extensions to include; pass an empty array for no filter
    
*   `entries` — output array that will be filled with names (no directory prefix)
    

**Example**

**Filtered example**

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#bool-delete_file-const-string-and-in-path)

`bool delete_file(const string &in path)`

Deletes a file.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#bool-delete_directory-const-string-and-in-path)

`bool delete_directory(const string &in path)`

Deletes a directory. Depending on configuration, the directory may need to be empty.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#example-test-script)

Example Test Script

A simple AngelScript example that exercises all functions:

[PreviousNet API](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api)
[NextExtended Math API](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/extended-math-api)

Last updated 22 days ago

*   [Overview](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#overview)
    
*   [Path Rules](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#path-rules)
    
*   [Global Functions](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#global-functions)
    
*   [Example Test Script](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/file-system#example-test-script)

    /folder/file.txt
    C:\temp\log.txt

Copy

    ..

    bool ok = create_file("data/info.txt", "Hello World!");

Copy

    bool ok = create_directory("data/logs");

Copy

    bool ok = read_file("data/info.txt", text);
    if (ok)
    {
        log("File contents: " + text);
    }

Copy

    if (does_file_exist("data/info.txt"))
    {
        log("File exists");
    }

Copy

    array<string> entries;
    array<string> noFilter; // empty
    
    bool ok = query_directory("data", true, true, noFilter, entries);
    if (ok)
    {
        for (uint i = 0; i < entries.length(); ++i)
        {
            log("Entry: " + entries[i]);
        }
    }

Copy

    array<string> exts = { ".json" };
    array<string> jsonFiles;
    
    bool ok = query_directory("data", false, true, exts, jsonFiles);
    if (ok)
    {
        for (uint i = 0; i < jsonFiles.length(); ++i)
        {
            log("JSON: " + jsonFiles[i]);
        }
    }

Copy

    bool ok = delete_file("data/old.txt");

Copy

    bool ok = delete_directory("data/temp");

Copy

    int main()
    {
        log("=== AS FS TEST START ===");
    
        // 1) Create a directory
        bool ok = create_directory("fs_tests");
        log("create_directory: " + string(ok ? "true" : "false"));
    
        // 2) Create a file
        ok = create_file("fs_tests/test.txt", "Hello from AngelScript FS API!\n");
        log("create_file: " + string(ok ? "true" : "false"));
    
        // 3) Read it back
        string data;
        ok = read_file("fs_tests/test.txt", data);
        log("read_file: " + string(ok ? "true" : "false"));
        if (ok)
            log("data = " + data);
    
        // 4) Check existence
        bool exists = does_file_exist("fs_tests/test.txt");
        log("does_file_exist: " + string(exists ? "true" : "false"));
    
        // 5) Query directory
        array<string> entries;
        array<string> noFilter;
        ok = query_directory("fs_tests", true, true, noFilter, entries);
        log("query_directory: " + string(ok ? "true" : "false"));
        if (ok)
        {
            for (uint i = 0; i < entries.length(); ++i)
                log("entry: " + entries[i]);
        }
    
        // 6) Delete file + directory
        ok = delete_file("fs_tests/test.txt");
        log("delete_file: " + string(ok ? "true" : "false"));
    
        ok = delete_directory("fs_tests");
        log("delete_directory: " + string(ok ? "true" : "false"));
    
        log("=== AS FS TEST END ===");
        return 1; // keep script loaded
    }

---

# Input API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The Input API provides full access to mouse, keyboard, and scroll states from AngelScript. All functions are **safe** — no pointers or raw memory are exposed to scripts.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#mouse)

📍 Mouse

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#get-mouse-position)

Get Mouse Position

Copy

    void get_mouse_pos(float &out x, float &out y)

Returns the current mouse position **within the viewport**.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#get-mouse-position-relative-to-desktop)

Get Mouse Position Relative To Desktop

Copy

    void get_mouse_pos_desktop(float &out x, float &out y)

Returns the absolute mouse position in **desktop coordinates** (OS-space).

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#get-mouse-movement-delta)

Get Mouse Movement Delta

Copy

    void get_mouse_delta(float &out dx, float &out dy)

Returns the **delta movement** of the mouse since the last frame (viewport space).

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#get-mouse-movement-delta-relative-to-desktop)

Get Mouse Movement Delta Relative To Desktop

Copy

    void get_mouse_delta_desktop(float &out dx, float &out dy)

Returns the **desktop-space delta** of mouse movement since the last frame.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#was-mouse-movement-received)

Was Mouse Movement Received

Returns `true` if any mouse movement has been received during this frame.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#get-scroll-delta)

Get Scroll Delta

Returns the scroll wheel delta value for the current frame.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#is-hovered-over-region)

Is Hovered Over Region

Returns `true` if the mouse is hovering over a given rectangular region.

*   `(x, y)` — Top-left corner of the region.
    
*   `(w, h)` — Width and height of the region.
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#keyboard)

⌨️ Keyboard

Keyboard functions use **virtual key (VK)** codes (standard Windows-style, e.g., `0x41` = A).

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#key-state-queries)

Key State Queries

Each of the following functions takes an `int vk` (the virtual key code):

Function

Description

`key_down`

Returns `true` if the key is currently held down.

`key_raw_down`

Returns raw (unfiltered) down state.

`key_fired`

Returns `true` if the key transitioned from up→down this frame (WinProc like input for input boxes, etc).

`key_toggle`

Returns toggle state (for keys like CapsLock).

`key_singlepress`

True only once per press event (useful for UI).

`key_prev_down`

Returns `true` if the key was down in the previous frame.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#get-key-state)

Get Key State

Fetches **all key state flags at once** for the specified key.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#get-keys-down)

Get Keys Down

Fills an array with the **virtual key codes** of all keys currently held down.

Example:

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#text-input)

🔡 Text Input

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#get-latest-key-input)

Get Latest Key Input

Returns a string containing the most recently typed characters since the last frame. Use this for text fields or console input.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#get-key-name-by-vk)

Get Key Name By VK

Returns a **human-readable name** for the specified virtual key code. Example: `get_key_name(0x41)` → `"A"`

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#notes)

🧠 Notes

*   All keyboard queries use the Windows-style **VK codes** (`0x01` = LMB, `0x41` = A, `0x1B` = ESC, etc.).
    
*   Mouse functions operate in **viewport space** unless the “desktop” variant is used.
    
*   Functions are designed to be **safe and lightweight** — they only read internal copies of state.
    
*   You can safely call any of these from UI, game logic, or render scripts.
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#example-usage)

🧩 Example Usage

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#version)

Version

[PreviousRender API](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/render-api)
[NextProc API](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/proc-api)

Last updated 19 days ago

*   [📍 Mouse](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#mouse)
    
*   [⌨️ Keyboard](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#keyboard)
    
*   [🔡 Text Input](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#text-input)
    
*   [🧠 Notes](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/input-api#notes)

    void update_ui()
    {
        float mx, my;
        get_mouse_pos(mx, my);
    
        if (is_hovered(100,100,200,80))
            draw_rect_filled(100,100,200,80, 50,120,255,180, 6.0f, RR_TOP_LEFT|RR_TOP_RIGHT);
    
        if (key_fired(0x1B)) // ESC key
            print("Escape pressed!\n");
    
        string input = get_recent_key_input();
        if (input.length() > 0)
            draw_text("Typed: " + input, mx + 10, my + 10,
                      255,255,255,255, get_font18(), TE_NONE, 0,0,0,0, 0.0f, true);
    }

# CS2 Extended API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

This API is available in both the Uni API and the CS2 product.

In the CS2 product, all standard Proc API functions are supported **except**:

*   Process referencing by PID/name
    
*   Engine-specific helpers
    
*   Virtual memory allocation (`alloc_vm` / `free_vm`)
    

On CS2 Product, `ref_process()` always returns the **CS2 process only**, so it is used like:

Copy

    proc_t cs2 = ref_process();  // for CS2 Product only

There is **no memory allocation API** exposed in the CS2 product.

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/cs2-extended-api#uint64-proc_t-cs2_get_interface-uint64-module_base-const-string-and-in-name-const)

🔗 `uint64 proc_t::cs2_get_interface(uint64 module_base, const string &in name) const`

Resolves a **CreateInterface-style** interface exported by a CS2 module.

Copy

    uint64 proc_t::cs2_get_interface(
        uint64 module_base,
        const string &in name
    ) const

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/cs2-extended-api#parameters)

**Parameters**

*   `**module_base**` Base address of the module containing `CreateInterface` (e.g. `"tier0.dll"`).
    
*   `**name**` Interface name, e.g. `"VEngineCvar007"`.
    

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/cs2-extended-api#returns)

**Returns**

*   An **absolute pointer** to the resolved interface.
    
*   `0` if the interface wasn’t found.
    

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/cs2-extended-api#array-less-than-dictionary-greater-than-proc_t-cs2_get_schema_dump-const)

🧬 `array<dictionary@>@ proc_t::cs2_get_schema_dump() const`

Dumps every field exposed by the **Source 2 Schema System** for `client.dll`.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/cs2-extended-api#return-format)

**Return Format**

Returns an array of dictionaries. Each element has:

Key

Type

Description

`"name"`

string

`"ClassName::fieldName"` (UTF-8)

`"offset"`

int64

Field offset relative to the class base

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/cs2-extended-api#example-element)

**Example element**

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/cs2-extended-api#full-example-interface-lookup--schema-dump)

🧪 Full Example — Interface Lookup + Schema Dump

[PreviousBit Reinterpret Helpers](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers)

Last updated 13 days ago

*   [🔗 uint64 proc\_t::cs2\_get\_interface(uint64 module\_base, const string &in name) const](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/cs2-extended-api#uint64-proc_t-cs2_get_interface-uint64-module_base-const-string-and-in-name-const)
    
*   [🧬 array<dictionary@>@ proc\_t::cs2\_get\_schema\_dump() const](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/cs2-extended-api#array-less-than-dictionary-greater-than-proc_t-cs2_get_schema_dump-const)
    
*   [🧪 Full Example — Interface Lookup + Schema Dump](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/cs2-extended-api#full-example-interface-lookup--schema-dump)
    

Copy

    array<dictionary@>@ proc_t::cs2_get_schema_dump() const

Copy

    {
      "name": "C_BaseEntity::m_iHealth",
      "offset": 16
    }

Copy

    void dump_schema(proc_t cs2)
    {
        array<dictionary@>@ entries = cs2.cs2_get_schema_dump();
        if (entries is null || entries.length() == 0)
        {
            log("[AS] schema dump empty");
            return;
        }
        
        log("[AS] Dumping " + entries.length() + " schema fields...");
        
        for (uint i = 0; i < entries.length(); i++)
        {
            dictionary@ d = entries[i];
            if (d is null)
                continue;
            
            string name;
            int64  offset;
            
            d.get("name",   name);
            d.get("offset", offset);
            
            log(name + " @ 0x" + formatUInt(uint(offset), "0H", 8));
        }
        
        log("[AS] Schema dump complete.");
        
        // Format example:
        // CPulse_CallInfo::m_nEditorNodeID @ 0x00000010
    }
    
    int main()
    {
        proc_t cs2 = ref_process("cs2.exe");
        // If you're using the CS2 Product edition, call ref_process() with no arguments.
        if (!cs2.alive())
        {
            log("[AS] cs2.exe not found");
            return 0;
        }
        
        uint64 tierBase, tierSize;
        if (!cs2.get_module("tier0.dll", tierBase, tierSize))
        {
            log("[AS] tier0.dll not found");
            return 0;
        }
        
        uint64 iface = cs2.cs2_get_interface(tierBase, "VEngineCvar007");
        
        if (iface == 0)
        {
            log("[AS] interface not found!");
            return 0;
        }
        
        log("VEngineCvar007 interface at 0x" + formatUInt(iface, "0H", 16));
            
        dump_schema(cs2);
        return 1;
    }

---

# Bit Reinterpret Helpers | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The **Bit Reinterpret Helpers** allow scripts to inspect the raw bit-pattern of numeric values by converting them into a `uint32`.

These functions **do not convert or scale values** — they reinterpret the raw memory bits of the input

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-f_to_u32-float-f)

`uint32 f_to_u32(float f)`

Returns the raw 32-bit IEEE-754 representation of a float.

Copy

    uint32 bits = f_to_u32(1.0f);     // 0x3F800000

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-u8_to_u32-uint8-v)

`uint32 u8_to_u32(uint8 v)`

Reinterprets a `uint8` as a `uint32`.

Copy

    uint32 bits = u8_to_u32(255);     // 0x000000FF

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-u16_to_u32-uint16-v)

`uint32 u16_to_u32(uint16 v)`

Reinterprets the lower 16 bits of a `uint16` as a 32-bit integer.

Copy

    uint32 bits = u16_to_u32(50000);

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-u64_to_u32-uint64-v)

`uint32 u64_to_u32(uint64 v)`

Returns the **lower 32 bits** of a 64-bit unsigned integer.

Copy

    uint32 bits = u64_to_u32(0x1122334455667788);

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-i8_to_u32-int8-v)

`uint32 i8_to_u32(int8 v)`

Reinterprets a signed 8-bit integer as a 32-bit unsigned integer.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-i16_to_u32-int16-v)

`uint32 i16_to_u32(int16 v)`

Reinterprets a signed 16-bit integer as 32 bits.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-i32_to_u32-int32-v)

`uint32 i32_to_u32(int32 v)`

Reinterprets a signed 32-bit integer as an unsigned one **without numerical conversion**.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-i64_to_u32-int64-v)

`uint32 i64_to_u32(int64 v)`

Returns the lower 32 bits of a 64-bit signed integer.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-d_to_u32-double-v)

`uint32 d_to_u32(double v)`

Returns the first 4 bytes of a 64-bit double (the lower half of the binary representation).

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#float-bits_to_float-uint-raw)

`**float bits_to_float(uint raw)**`

Reinterprets a 32-bit unsigned integer as an IEEE-754 `float`.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#double-bits_to_double-uint64-raw)

`**double bits_to_double(uint64 raw)**`

Reinterprets a 64-bit unsigned integer as an IEEE-754 `double`.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint-float_to_bits-float-value)

`**uint float_to_bits(float value)**`

Returns the exact 32-bit IEEE-754 bit pattern of a `float`.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint64-double_to_bits-double-value)

`**uint64 double_to_bits(double value)**`

Returns the exact 64-bit IEEE-754 bit pattern of a `double`.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#float-u32_to_f-uint-raw)

`**float u32_to_f(uint raw)**`

Convenience alias for `bits_to_float(raw)`.

[PreviousUtilities](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/utilities)
[NextCS2 Extended API](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/cs2-extended-api)

Last updated 2 days ago

Copy

    uint32 bits = i8_to_u32(-5);      // 0xFFFFFFFB

Copy

    uint32 bits = i16_to_u32(-1234);

Copy

    uint32 bits = i32_to_u32(-1);     // 0xFFFFFFFF

Copy

    uint32 bits = i64_to_u32(-1);     // 0xFFFFFFFF

Copy

    uint32 bits = d_to_u32(3.1415926535);

Copy

    float f = bits_to_float(0x3F800000);    // 1.0f

Copy

    double d = bits_to_double(0x400921FB54442D18);   // 3.141592653589793

Copy

    uint bits = float_to_bits(1.0f);        // 0x3F800000

Copy

    uint64 bits = double_to_bits(3.141592653589793); // 0x400921FB54442D18

Copy

    float f = u32_to_f(0xBF800000);         // -1.0f

---

# System API (CPU & Disassembly) | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

Low-level CPU information, high-precision timing, and full multi-instruction x64 disassembly using **Zydis**.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#overview)

📌 Overview


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The System API provides:

*   **CPU Information**
    
*   **High-Resolution Performance Timers**
    
*   **x64 Instruction Disassembly** using **Zydis**
    
*   Full operand breakdown: registers, memory operands, immediates, pointer operands, etc.
    

All functions are **global** inside AngelScript.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#available-functions)

📘 Available Functions


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#cpu-information)

🔧 CPU Information

Function

Returns

Description

`string cpu_vendor()`

`"AuthenticAMD"`, `"GenuineIntel"`

CPU vendor ID

`string cpu_brand()`

`"AMD Ryzen 9 7900X 12-Core Processor"`

Human-readable CPU model

* * *

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#timing)

⏱ Timing

Function

Returns

Description

`uint64 rdtsc()`

Raw CPU timestamp counter

Fast but CPU-frequency dependent

`int64 perf_time()`

High-resolution performance counter

Use with `perf_frequency()`

`int64 perf_frequency()`

Ticks per second

For converting perf\_time → seconds

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#example-timing-a-loop)

📌 Example (timing a loop)

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#zydis-disassembly-api)

🧩 Zydis Disassembly API


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#functions)

Functions

Function

Returns

Description

`void zydis_disasm(const array<uint8>& in bytes, array<dictionary@>& out out_insts)`

`array<dictionary@>`

Full decode starting at RIP=0

`void zydis_disasm(const array<uint8>& in bytes, uint64 runtime_rip, array<dictionary@>& out out_insts)`

`array<dictionary@>`

Full decode with custom RIP

Both return a **list of instructions**, where each item is a **dictionary** with metadata and operand array.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#instruction-structure-disasm_instruction_t)

🧱 Instruction Structure (`disasm_instruction_t`)


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Each instruction dictionary contains:

Key

Type

Description

`"runtime_address"`

`int64`

Instruction RIP

`"length"`

`int64`

Size in bytes

`"mnemonic"`

`string`

`"mov"`, `"push"`, `"lea"`

`"text"`

`string`

Full Intel disassembly text

`"operand_count"`

`int64`

Total operands

`"operand_count_visible"`

`int64`

Non-hidden operands

`"operands"`

`array<dictionary@>`

List of operand tables

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#operand-structure-operand_t)

🔍 Operand Structure (`operand_t`)


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Each operand dictionary contains:

Key

Type

Example

Notes

`"id"`

`int64`

`0`

Operand index

`"type"`

`string`

`"reg"` / `"mem"` / `"imm"` / `"ptr"`

Operand type

`"visibility"`

`string`

`"explicit"` / `"hidden"`

`"size"`

`int64`

`64`

Bit size

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#register-operand)

Register operand

Key

Type

Description

`"reg_name"`

`string`

`"rax"`, `"rcx"`, `"xmm0"`

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#memory-operand)

Memory operand

Key

Type

Description

`"mem_segment"`

`string`

`"ss"`

`"mem_base"`

`string`

`"rbp"`

`"mem_index"`

`string`

`"rax"` or ""

`"mem_scale"`

`int64`

Scale (1,2,4,8)

`"mem_has_displacement"`

`int64` (0/1)

Whether displacement exists

`"mem_displacement"`

`int64`

Signed displacement

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#immediate-operand)

Immediate operand

Key

Type

Description

`"imm_is_signed"`

`int64` (0/1)

Signed flag

`"imm_is_relative"`

`int64` (0/1)

Is relative jump?

`"imm_value"`

`int64`

Immediate value

`"imm_absolute_address"`

`int64`

Computed RIP + relOffset

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#pointer-operand)

Pointer operand

Key

Type

Description

`"ptr_segment"`

`int64`

`"ptr_offset"`

`int64`

📅 Date & Time API


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Provides local date/time information, including readable names, 12-hour formatting, and Unix timestamps.

### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#functions-1)

🧭 Functions

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#dictionary-get_datetime)

`**dictionary@ get_datetime()**`

Returns a dictionary with the following keys:

Key

Type

Description

`"year"`

int

e.g. 2025

`"month"`

int

1–12

`"day"`

int

1–31

`"hour"`

int

0–23

`"minute"`

int

0–59

`"second"`

int

0–59

`"msec"`

int

0–999

`"day_name"`

string

`"Monday"`, `"Tuesday"`, ...

`"month_name"`

string

`"January"`, `"February"`, ...

`"hour12"`

int

1–12

`"ampm"`

string

`"AM"` or `"PM"`

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#uint64-get_timestamp)

`**uint64 get_timestamp()**`

Returns a **Unix timestamp** in **UTC**, measured in seconds since `1970-01-01`.

Copy

    int64 freq = perf_frequency();
    int64 t0   = perf_time();
    
    for (uint i = 0; i < 1000000; i++) { }
    
    int64 t1 = perf_time();
    double dt_sec = double(t1 - t0) / double(freq);
    
    log("Elapsed seconds: " + dt_sec);

Copy

    int main()
    {
        log("=== AS SYSTEM / ZYDIS FULL TEST START ===");
    
        // CPU info
        log("CPU Vendor: " + cpu_vendor());
        log("CPU Brand : " + cpu_brand());
    
        // Timing test
        int64 freq = perf_frequency();
        int64 t0   = perf_time();
    
        uint64 sum = 0;
        for (uint i = 0; i < 1000000; i++) sum += i;
    
        int64 t1 = perf_time();
        log("perf_frequency (ticks/sec): " + freq);
        log("perf_time delta seconds   : " + double(t1 - t0) / double(freq));
    
        log("RDTSC: " + rdtsc());
    
        // Example code to disassemble
        array<uint8> bytes = {
            0x55,                    // push rbp
            0x48, 0x89, 0xE5,        // mov rbp, rsp
            0x48, 0x83, 0xEC, 0x30   // sub rsp, 0x30
        };
    
        array<dictionary@> ins;
        zydis_disasm(bytes, 0x140000000, ins);
    
        log("=== ZYDIS TEST (HARDCODED BYTES) ===");
        for (uint i = 0; i < ins.length(); i++)
        {
            dictionary@ inst = ins[i];
    
            int64 addr; 
            inst.get("runtime_address", addr);
    
            string text;
            inst.get("text", text);
    
            log(formatInt(addr, "0x%X") + ": " + text);
        }
    
        log("=== AS SYSTEM / ZYDIS FULL TEST END ===");
        return 1;
    }

Copy

    === AS SYSTEM / ZYDIS FULL TEST START ===
    CPU Vendor: AuthenticAMD
    CPU Brand : AMD Ryzen 9 7900X 12-Core Processor
    
    perf_frequency (ticks/sec): 10000000
    perf_time delta seconds : 0.0094
    RDTSC: 161134003150540
    
    === ZYDIS TEST (HARDCODED BYTES) ===
    0x140000000: push rbp
    0x140000001: mov rbp, rsp
    0x140000004: sub rsp, 0x30
    
    === AS SYSTEM / ZYDIS FULL TEST END ===

Copy

    int main()
    {
        dictionary@ dt = get_datetime();
        
        int year, month, day, hour12, minute;
        string dayName, monthName, ampm;
        
        dt.get("year", year);
        dt.get("month", month);
        dt.get("day", day);
        dt.get("hour12", hour12);
        dt.get("minute", minute);
        dt.get("day_name", dayName);
        dt.get("month_name", monthName);
        dt.get("ampm", ampm);
        
        log("Today is: " + dayName + ", " + monthName + " " + day + ", " + year);
        log("Local Time: " +
        hour12 +
        ":" +
        (minute < 10 ? "0" + formatInt(minute) : formatInt(minute)) +
        " " + ampm);
        
        uint64 ts = get_timestamp();
        log("Unix Timestamp: " + ts);
        return 1;
    }

# Extended Math API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

This API provides vectors, quaternions, matrices, math constants, and helper functions found in modern game engines.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#contents)

📘 Contents


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Math Constants
    
*   Global Math Helpers
    
*   vector2
    
*   vector3
    
*   quaternion
    
*   matrix4x4
    
*   mat4 Namespace
    

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#math-constants)

🔢 **Math Constants**


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

These are available globally:

Name

Value

`M_PI`

3.141592653589793

`M_TAU`

6.283185307179586 (2π)

`M_PI_2`

π/2

`M_PI_4`

π/4

`DEG2RAD`

π/180

`RAD2DEG`

180/π

`PI_OVER_180`

π/180

`INV_PI_OVER_180`

180/π

`M_ZERO`

0

`M_ONE`

1

`M_EPSILON`

0.000001

Usage:

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#global-math-helpers)

🛠 **Global Math Helpers**


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#clamp-x-min-max)

✔ clamp(x, min, max)

Clamps a value between two bounds.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#saturate-x)

✔ saturate(x)

Clamps value to `[0,1]`.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#sign-x)

✔ sign(x)

Returns `-1`, `0`, or `1`.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#round-x-round_up-x-round_down-x)

✔ round(x), round\_up(x), round\_down(x)

Standard rounding helpers.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#fract-x)

✔ fract(x)

Fractional part (always 0–1, even for negatives).

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#wrap-x-min-max)

✔ wrap(x, min, max)

Wraps a number into a cyclic range.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#lerp-a-b-t)

✔ lerp(a, b, t)

Linear interpolation.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#inverse_lerp-a-b-v)

✔ inverse\_lerp(a, b, v)

Inverse of `lerp`.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#remap-a1-b1-a2-b2-v)

✔ remap(a1, b1, a2, b2, v)

Maps a value from one range to another.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#smoothstep-edge0-edge1-x)

✔ smoothstep(edge0, edge1, x)

Smooth Hermite interpolation.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#step-edge-x)

✔ step(edge, x)

Returns 0 if x < edge, else 1.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#is_nan-x-is_inf-x)

✔ is\_nan(x), is\_inf(x)

Checks numeric state.

* * *

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#vector2)

🟦 **vector2**


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A 2D double-precision vector.

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#create)

✔ Create

#### 

[](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#fields)

    local R = mat4.rotate_euler(0, 90, 0)
